Definition of a Garment and Conditions of Loss
Defines what counts as a garment and when one is considered lacking

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define what constitutes a garment for covering the awrah and identify the conditions under which a person is considered 'lacking' a garment.

Core Idea
Any material that covers the awrah qualifies as a garment, even grass or mud, but not transparent materials.

The term 'thawb' (garment) in the context of prayer has a broad definition. Al-Bahr al-Raiq explains that covering the awrah is a condition for valid prayer, and if no conventional garment is available, one must use any available material. This lesson focuses on the definition and the conditions that determine when a person is truly without covering.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of 'garment'
The text defines 'thawb' as anything that covers most of the awrah, including silk, grass, plants, leaves, or mud. Glass and transparent materials are excluded.
2
Determine the scope of 'lacking'
Lack (ʿadam) is established by non-existence in one's possession and by non-permissibility (e.g., no permission to use). If a garment is permissible but not owned, the person is still considered able.
3
Apply the condition to a scenario
If a person has access to a garment (e.g., borrowed), he must use it. Praying naked when he could have obtained a covering invalidates the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والصلاة قاعداً مومياً بركوع وسجود وهو أفضل من القيام بركوع وسجود والنية يسل فإنه يصلي قاعداً مومياً لأن ترك السجود أهون من الصلاة الحدث، ألا ترى أن ترك السجود جائز حالة الاختيار في التطوع على الدابة، ومع الحدث لا يجوز بحال. فإن قام وقرأ وركع ثم قعد وأومأ للسجود جاز لما قلنا والأول أفضل، وكذا شيخ لا يقدر على القراءة قائماً ويقدر عليها قاعداً يصلي قاعداً لأنه يجوز حالة الاختيار في النفل ولا يجوز ترك القراءة بحال، ولو صلى في الفصلين قائماً مع الحدث وترك القراءة لم يجز . قوله : ( ولو عدم ثوباً صلى قاعداً مومياً بركوع وسجود وهو أفضل من القيام بركوع وسجود) لما عن أنس أن أصحاب رسول الله وركبوا في السفينة فانكسرت بهم فخرجوا من البحر عراة فصلوا قعوداً بإيماء. أراد بالثوب ما يستر عامة عورته ولو حريراً أو حشيشاً أو نباتاً أو كلاً أو طيناً يلطخ به عورته ويبقى عليه حتى يصلي لا الزجاج الذي يصف ما تحته. والعدم المذكور يثبت بعدم الوجود في ملكه وبعدم الإباحة له حتى لو أبيح له ثوب تثبت القدرة به على الأصح ، فلو صلى عارياً لم يجز كالمتيمم إذا أبيح له الماء. وعن محمد في العريان يعده صاحبه أنه يعطيه الثوب إذا صلى فإنه ينتظره ولا يصلي عرياناً وإن خاف فوت الوقت. كذا في السراج الوهاج وفي القنية عن أبي حنيفة : ينتظره ما لم يخف فوت الوقت وأبو يوسف مع أبي حنيفة. وينبغي ترجيحه قياساً على المتيمم إذا كان يرجو الماء في آخره. في الصلاة قاعداً فشمل ما إذا كان نهاراً أو ليلاً في بيت أو صحراء وهو الصحيح كما بينه في منية المصلي، ومن المشايخ من خصه بالنهار، أما في الليل فيصلي قائماً لأن ظلمة الليل تستر عورته قال في الذخيرة وهذا ليس بمرضي لأن الستر الذي يحصل في ظلمة الليل لا عبرة به ألا ترى أن حالة القدرة على الثوب إذا صلى عرياناً في ظلمة الليل لا يجوز فصار وجوده وعدمه بمنزلة واحدة ا هـ. وتعقبه في شرح منية المصلي بأن الاستشهاد المذكور غير متجه للفرق بين حالة الاختيار وحالة الاضطرار وأطال إلى أن قال : ويؤيده ما أخرجه عبد الرزاق سئل علي رضي الله عنه عن صلاة العريان قال: إن كان حيث يراه الناس صلى جالساً، وإن كان حيث لا يراه الناس صلى قائماً. وهو وإن كان سنده ضعيفاً فلا يقصر عن إفادة الاستئناس وأما واقعة الصحابة المتقدمة فقد تطرق إليها احتمالات، إما لأنهم اختاروا الأولى لما فيه من تقليل الانكشاف أو لأنهم كانوا مترائين أو لم يكن ليلاً فسقط بها الاستدلال، ولم يبين المصنف صفة القعود للاختلاف فيها. ففي منية المصلي : يقعد كما يقعد في الصلاة. فعلى هذا يختلف في الرجل والمرأة، فهو يفترش وهي تتورك. وفي الذخيرة: يقعد ويمد وأطلق
And prayer sitting with gestures for bowing and prostration, and it is better than standing with bowing and prostration, and the intention... he prays sitting with gestures because leaving prostration is easier than praying with ritual impurity. Do you not see that leaving prostration is permissible in the state of choice in supererogatory prayers on a mount, but with ritual impurity it is not permissible under any circumstance. If he stood, recited, bowed, then sat down and gestured for prostration, it is permissible according to what we said, and the first is better. Similarly, an old man who cannot recite while standing but can while sitting, prays sitting because it is permissible in the state of choice in supererogatory prayers, and leaving recitation is never permissible. If he prays in both phases standing with impurity and leaving recitation, it is not permissible. His statement: (If he lacks a garment, he prays sitting with gestures for bowing and prostration, and it is better than standing with bowing and prostration) because of what is narrated from Anas that the companions of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) rode on a ship, and it broke with them, so they came out of the sea naked and prayed sitting with gestures. By 'garment' is meant what covers most of his awrah, even if it be silk, grass, plants, leaves, or mud with which he smears his awrah and remains on it until he prays, but not glass that reveals what is under it. The mentioned lack (of a garment) is established by the non-existence in his possession and by the non-permissibility for him; even if a garment is made permissible for him, ability is established with it according to the most correct view, so if he prays naked it is not valid, like the one performing tayammum when water is made permissible for him. According to Muhammad, regarding the naked person whose companion promises to give him a garment, he waits for him and does not pray naked even if he fears the time will pass. Likewise in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and in al-Qunyah from Abu Hanifah: He waits for him as long as he does not fear the time passing, and Abu Yusuf agrees with Abu Hanifah. And it is preferable to give preponderance to this view by analogy with the one performing tayammum if he hopes for water at the end of the time. His prayer sitting includes whether it is day or night, inside a house or in the desert, and this is the correct view as explained in Munyat al-Musalli. Some mashayikh restricted it to daytime, while at night he prays standing because the darkness of the night covers his awrah. Al-Dhakhirah said: This is not satisfactory because the covering obtained in the darkness of the night is not considered; do you not see that in the state of ability to have a garment, if he prays naked at night, it is not valid, so its existence and non-existence are alike. It was objected to in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli that the mentioned analogy is not appropriate for the distinction between the state of choice and the state of necessity, and he extended the discussion until he said: It is supported by what Abd al-Razzaq narrated: Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) was asked about the prayer of the naked man; he said: If he is where people see him, he prays sitting; if he is where people do not see him, he prays standing. Even though its chain is weak, it is not less than providing comfort. As for the earlier incident of the companions, possibilities have been raised about it: either they chose the best because it minimizes exposure, or because they were visible to each other, or because it was not night, so the inference falls. The author did not specify the manner of sitting due to disagreement about it. In Munyat al-Musalli: He sits as he sits in prayer. On this basis, it differs for a man and a woman: he sits with iftirash, and she sits with tawarruk. In al-Dhakhirah: He sits and extends (his legs) and it is absolute.
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses the ruling for a person who has no garment to cover his awrah (al-ʿuryān). The matn (base text) states that such a person prays sitting with gestures (īmāʾ) for bowing and prostrating, and this is superior to standing with full bowing and prostration. The commentator expands with proof from the incident of the Prophet's companions who were shipwrecked and prayed naked while sitting. The reasoning given is that leaving prostration (by sitting) is a lesser loss than praying with ritual impurity (hadath), which is never allowed. The passage then defines what counts as a 'garment': anything that covers most of the awrah, even silk, grass, or mud, but not transparent material like glass. The loss of a garment can be due to lack of possession or lack of permission to use; if a garment is made permissible (e.g., someone offers to lend), the person is considered able and must pray clothed. A key intra-Hanafi dispute is whether one should wait for a promised garment: according to Muhammad (Ibn al-Hasan), one must wait even if the time may pass; according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, one waits only if there is no fear of time expiring. The commentator preponderates Muhammad's view by analogy with tayammum where one hopes for water. Another dispute concerns night-time darkness: some scholars say one may stand at night because darkness hides the awrah, but this is rejected because darkness does not actually cover; the ruling should be the same as daytime. The passage ends with a difference in how to sit: whether as in regular prayer (with iftirash for men, tawarruk for women) or simply extending the legs, and the author did not specify due to the ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
الثوب (al-thawb): Garment that covers the awrah; defined broadly to include any concealing material.
الإباحة (al-ibāhah): Permission to use something (here, a garment owned by another).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT considered a valid covering for the awrah according to the passage?
A) Mud smeared on the body
B) Grass woven together
C) A transparent plastic sheet
D) A silk cloth

Key Takeaway
A garment for prayer encompasses any opaque material that covers the awrah; loss is defined by lack of ownership and lack of permission.

intermediate
7 min
Waiting for a Promised Garment: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on waiting for a garment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the conflicting Hanafi views on whether a naked person should wait for a promised garment and identify the preponderant position.

Core Idea
Whether to wait for a garment depends on the risk of missing the prayer time; analogy to waiting for water in tayammum.

When a naked person is promised a garment by someone, should he wait for it or pray naked immediately? This lesson explores the disagreement between Muhammad ibn al-Hasan on one side and Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on the other. The commentator weighs in by qiyas with tayammum, indicating that waiting is required only if there is no fear of the time expiring.

Guided Path
1
State the views of the imams
Muhammad: He must wait even if the time passes. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: He waits only if he does not fear the time will expire.
2
Identify the analogy used
The commentator analogizes to tayammum: if one hopes for water at the end of the time, he delays tayammum. Similarly, waiting for a garment is like waiting for water.
3
Evaluate the tarjih
The commentator prefers the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as it balances the obligation to cover with the duty to pray on time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

القراءة بحال، ولو صلى في الفصلين قائماً مع الحدث وترك القراءة لم يجز . قوله : ( ولو عدم ثوباً صلى قاعداً مومياً بركوع وسجود وهو أفضل من القيام بركوع وسجود) لما عن أنس أن أصحاب رسول الله وركبوا في Checkpoint
According to the preponderant Hanafi view, when does a naked person wait for a promised garment?
A) Always, even if it means missing the prayer time.
B) Only if he does not fear that the prayer time will expire.
C) Only if the garment is made of silk.
D) Never; he must pray naked immediately.

Key Takeaway

Night vs. Day: The Naked Person's Prayer in Darkness
Refutation of night-time exception for naked prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi dispute on whether a naked person may stand to pray at night and justify the preponderant view.

Core Idea
Darkness does not constitute actual covering; the ruling for night prayer is the same as for daytime.

Some later Hanafi scholars argued that at night, because darkness hides the awrah, the person could stand and pray normally. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq rejects this distinction, citing the ruling of Ali (ra) and the principle that darkness does not provide legal cover. We will examine the arguments and why the commentator considers the night-day distinction unsatisfactory.

Guided Path
1
State the disputed view
Some mashayikh (scholars) said that at night the person may stand because darkness covers the awrah.
2
Present the refutation
Al-Dhakhirah argues that darkness does not actually cover: if a person has a garment, he cannot discard it and pray naked at night, so darkness has no legal effect.
3
Consider the narration from Ali
Ali (ra) is reported to have distinguished between being seen and not seen. The commentator notes this but weakens its chain, and notes that the incident of the companions occurred in daytime without such distinction.
4
Conclude the preponderant view
The correct view, supported by al-Dhakhirah and the majority, is that the ruling is the same for night and day: sit with gestures.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

المصلي بأن الاستشهاد المذكور غير متجه للفرق بين حالة الاختيار وحالة الاضطرار وأطال إلى أن قال : ويؤيده ما أخرجه عبد الرزاق سئل علي رضي الله عنه عن صلاة العريان قال: إن كان حيث يراه الناس صلى جالساً، وإن كان حيث لا يراه الناس صلى قائماً. وهو وإن كان سنده ضعيفاً فلا يقصر عن إفادة الاستئناس وأما واقعة الصحابة المتقدمة فقد تطرق إليها احتمالات، إما لأنهم اختاروا الأولى لما فيه من تقليل الانكشاف أو لأنهم كانوا مترائين أو لم يكن ليلاً فسقط بها الاستدلال، ولم يبين المصنف صفة القعود للاختلاف فيها. ففي منية المصلي : يقعد كما يقعد في الصلاة. فعلى هذا يختلف في الرجل والمرأة، فهو يفترش وهي تتورك. وفي الذخيرة: يقعد ويمد وأطلق
And prayer sitting with gestures for bowing and prostration, and it is better than standing with bowing and prostration, and the intention... he prays sitting with gestures because leaving prostration is easier than praying with ritual impurity. Do you not see that leaving prostration is permissible in the state of choice in supererogatory prayers on a mount, but with ritual impurity it is not permissible under any circumstance. If he stood, recited, bowed, then sat down and gestured for prostration, it is permissible according to what we said, and the first is better. Similarly, an old man who cannot recite while standing but can while sitting, prays sitting because it is permissible in the state of choice in supererogatory prayers, and leaving recitation is never permissible. If he prays in both phases standing with impurity and leaving recitation, it is not permissible. His statement: (If he lacks a garment, he prays sitting with gestures for bowing and prostration, and it is better than standing with bowing and prostration) because of what is narrated from Anas that the companions of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) rode on a ship, and it broke with them, so they came out of the sea naked and prayed sitting with gestures. By 'garment' is meant what covers most of his awrah, even if it be silk, grass, plants, leaves, or mud with which he smears his awrah and remains on it until he prays, but not glass that reveals what is under it. The mentioned lack (of a garment) is established by the non-existence in his possession and by the non-permissibility for him; even if a garment is made permissible for him, ability is established with it according to the most correct view, so if he prays naked it is not valid, like the one performing tayammum when water is made permissible for him. According to Muhammad, regarding the naked person whose companion promises to give him a garment, he waits for him and does not pray naked even if he fears the time will pass. Likewise in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and in al-Qunyah from Abu Hanifah: He waits for him as long as he does not fear the time passing, and Abu Yusuf agrees with Abu Hanifah. And it is preferable to give preponderance to this view by analogy with the one performing tayammum if he hopes for water at the end of the time. His prayer sitting includes whether it is day or night, inside a house or in the desert, and this is the correct view as explained in Munyat al-Musalli. Some mashayikh restricted it to daytime, while at night he prays standing because the darkness of the night covers his awrah. Al-Dhakhirah said: This is not satisfactory because the covering obtained in the darkness of the night is not considered; do you not see that in the state of ability to have a garment, if he prays naked at night, it is not valid, so its existence and non-existence are alike. It was objected to in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli that the mentioned analogy is not appropriate for the distinction between the state of choice and the state of necessity, and he extended the discussion until he said: It is supported by what Abd al-Razzaq narrated: Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) was asked about the prayer of the naked man; he said: If he is where people see him, he prays sitting; if he is where people do not see him, he prays standing. Even though its chain is weak, it is not less than providing comfort. As for the earlier incident of the companions, possibilities have been raised about it: either they chose the best because it minimizes exposure, or because they were visible to each other, or because it was not night, so the inference falls. The author did not specify the manner of sitting due to disagreement about it. In Munyat al-Musalli: He sits as he sits in prayer. On this basis, it differs for a man and a woman: he sits with iftirash, and she sits with tawarruk. In al-Dhakhirah: He sits and extends (his legs) and it is absolute.
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses the ruling for a person who has no garment to cover his awrah (al-ʿuryān). The matn (base text) states that such a person prays sitting with gestures (īmāʾ) for bowing and prostrating, and this is superior to standing with full bowing and prostration. The commentator expands with proof from the incident of the Prophet's companions who were shipwrecked and prayed naked while sitting. The reasoning given is that leaving prostration (by sitting) is a lesser loss than praying with ritual impurity (hadath), which is never allowed. The passage then defines what counts as a 'garment': anything that covers most of the awrah, even silk, grass, or mud, but not transparent material like glass. The loss of a garment can be due to lack of possession or lack of permission to use; if a garment is made permissible (e.g., someone offers to lend), the person is considered able and must pray clothed. A key intra-Hanafi dispute is whether one should wait for a promised garment: according to Muhammad (Ibn al-Hasan), one must wait even if the time may pass; according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, one waits only if there is no fear of time expiring. The commentator preponderates Muhammad's view by analogy with tayammum where one hopes for water. Another dispute concerns night-time darkness: some scholars say one may stand at night because darkness hides the awrah, but this is rejected because darkness does not actually cover; the ruling should be the same as daytime. The passage ends with a difference in how to sit: whether as in regular prayer (with iftirash for men, tawarruk for women) or simply extending the legs, and the author did not specify due to the ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
الظلمة (al-zulmah): Darkness; argued by some to cover the awrah, but rejected in the correct view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does al-Dhakhirah reject the night-time exception for the naked person's prayer?
A) Because darkness is not considered a legal covering.
B) Because the companions' incident occurred at night.
C) Because standing is always better.
D) Because the narration from Ali is strong.

Key Takeaway
Darkness does not count as covering; the naked person's prayer is the same by day and by night: sitting with gestures.

Sitting Posture for the Naked Person: A Minor Dispute
Dispute on sitting posture for naked prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two views on how the naked person should sit during prayer and explain the lack of a definitive specification.

Core Idea
The proper sitting posture for the naked person is disputed; some say regular prayer posture, others say extended legs.

The passage ends with a note on the manner of sitting. The author (al-Marghinani?) did not specify because of disagreement. Munyat al-Musalli holds that he sits as in regular prayer (iftirash for men, tawarruk for women), while al-Dhakhirah says he sits with legs extended (madd). This lesson explores the two positions and why no definitive choice was made.

Guided Path
1
State the two views
Munyat al-Musalli: He sits as he normally would in prayer (men iftirash, women tawarruk). Al-Dhakhirah: He sits and extends his legs (tarbi'? 'madd').
2
Identify the basis for each
The first view tries to maintain the regular form as much as possible. The second view prioritizes covering by bringing the legs together to conceal the awrah further.
3
Note the author's restraint
The author of the base text (Kanz al-Daqaiq) did not specify the posture, leaving it open due to the ikhtilaf.

الافتراش (al-iftirāsh): Sitting posture for men in prayer: sitting on the left foot, right foot upright.
التورك (al-tawarruk): Sitting posture for women in prayer: sitting on the left buttock, legs out to the right.

Preferred Posture for a Naked Person in Prayer
Debate on best sitting posture for a naked person to maximize covering of 'awrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi view on the preferred posture for a naked person in prayer and explain the legal reasoning behind why sitting is better than standing.

Core Idea
Covering the 'awrah is an absolute obligation; sitting is better even if standing completes the pillars.

When a person has no clothing and must pray naked, the question arises: is it better to stand or sit? The Hanafi school discusses this in detail, weighing the obligation of covering the private parts against the performance of the prayer's pillars. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and addresses a critical objection about those who can only gesture.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and the Preference
Read the passage to determine which posture is preferred and which is merely permissible. Note that sitting is said to be 'better' (أفضل) than standing, but standing is still allowed.
The preference is based on maximizing covering of the 'awrah.
2
Analyze the Reason (Ta'lil) for the Preference
The text states that covering the 'awrah is an absolute obligation (فرض مطلق), while the pillars of prayer are only obligations within the prayer (فرائض الصلاة). Since sitting allows better covering, it takes priority.
This is a weighing of two obligations: a general one (covering) vs. specific prayer pillars.
3
Examine the Objection
A hypothetical objector argues that if the permission to abandon covering is only to complete the three pillars, then the one who gestures while standing does not actually complete the pillars properly. Therefore, standing should not be allowed for the gesturing person.
The objection uses analogical reasoning (qiyas) from the rules of the sick person's prayer.
4
Evaluate the Objection's Impact
The author raises the objection but does not refute it explicitly. He had already stated his preference for sitting. The objection highlights a potential inconsistency but does not overturn the preferred view.
This shows that scholarship considers counterarguments even when they don't change the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذي يظهر ترجيح الأول وأنه أولى لأنه يحصل به من المبالغة في الستر ما لا يحصل بالهيئة المذكورة مع خلو هذه الهيئة عن فعل ما ليس بأولى وهو مد رجليه إلى القبلة من غير ضرورة، والحاصل أن القعود على هيئة متعينة ليس بمتعين بل يجوز كيفما كان، وإنما كان القعود أفضل من القيام لأن ستر العورة أهم من أداء الأركان لأنه فرض مطلقاً والأركان فرائض الصلاة لا غير وقد أتى ببدلها. وإنما كان القيام جائزاً لأنه وإن ترك فرض الستر فقد كمل الأركان الثلاثة وبه حاجة إلى تكميلها. كذا في البدائع. ولقائل أن يقول : ينبغي على هذا أن لا يجوز الإيماء قائماً لأن تجويز ترك فرض الستر إنما كان لأجل تكميل الأركان الثلاثة والمومىء بهما قائماً لم يحرزهما على وجه الكمال أن القيام إنما شرع لتحصيلهما على وجه الكمال على ما صرحوا به في صلاة المريض أنه لو قدر على القيام دون الركوع والسجود أومأ قاعداً وسقط عنه القيام.
And it appears that the first is preferred and that it is better because through it is achieved such covering of the private parts as is not achieved by the mentioned posture, along with the absence in this posture of committing an act that is not better, namely stretching his legs toward the qibla without necessity. The conclusion is that sitting in a specific posture is not required; rather it is permissible in any manner. And indeed sitting is better than standing because covering the private parts is more important than performing the pillars, because it is an absolute obligation, while the pillars are only obligations of the prayer, and he has performed their substitutes. And indeed standing is permissible because even though he abandons the obligation of covering, he has completed the three pillars and had need to complete them. Thus in al-Bada'i'. And someone may say: According to this, it is not permissible to make gestures while standing, because the permission to abandon the obligation of covering was only for the sake of completing the three pillars, and the one who gestures with both [hands] while standing does not achieve them completely, because standing was legislated only to achieve them completely, as they explicitly stated in the prayer of the sick: if he is able to stand but not bow and prostrate, he gestures sitting, and standing is waived for him.
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with reasoning (ta'lil) regarding the best posture for a person who has no clothing and must pray naked. The author, al-Zayla'i, after presenting the view from al-Dhakhira that the person should sit with legs extended towards the qibla, states that the preferred view is that sitting with legs extended is better because it provides more covering of the private parts. He explains that sitting is better than standing because covering the 'awrah is a fard muthaq (absolute obligation) while the pillars of prayer are only fara'id within prayer, and sitting without standing is a substitute for the pillars (since he cannot stand). Standing is only permissible because he completes the three pillars (intention, takbir, and qiyam?) but he abandons covering. Then an objection is raised: if the reason for allowing the omission of covering is to complete the pillars, then the one who gestures (i.e., cannot fully perform ruku' and sujud) should not be allowed to stand because he does not actually complete the pillars; analogizing to the sick person who sits to gesture. This objection is left for consideration, but the author's earlier preference for sitting is upheld.

Key Terms
عورة ('awrah): The private parts that must be covered in prayer; for a man, from navel to knee.
إيماء (ima'): Gesturing with the head or body in lieu of bowing and prostrating when unable to perform them fully.
فرض مطلق (fard mutlaq): An absolute obligation that applies at all times, not conditional on the act of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is sitting better than standing for a naked person in prayer?
A) Because standing is not allowed at all
B) Because covering the 'awrah is more important than the pillar of standing
C) Because the person cannot stand due to illness
D) Because the person must cover his private parts with his hands

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, covering the 'awrah takes precedence over performing the prayer in the usual standing posture; therefore, a naked person should sit to maximize covering.

Partial Covering of 'Awrah: Front or Back?
Two opinions on priority of covering private parts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two opinions within the Hanafi school on which private part to cover when only one can be covered, and explain the reasoning behind each.

Core Idea
When cloth is insufficient, covering the front is preferred because it faces the qibla and has no natural cover; the back is more shameful during bowing.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario in the prayer of a person who has only enough cloth to cover one of the two private parts. The Hanafi school presents two reasoned opinions, both grounded in considerations of modesty and exposure. By understanding the reasoning, you will appreciate how legal rulings are derived from underlying values.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and general obligation
The passage begins by stating that if one has cloth to cover the smaller 'awrah (genitals) and does not, the prayer is invalid. Then it cites a ruling that if one can cover part of the 'awrah, he must use it and cover both front and back. The specific case is when only one part can be covered.
Smaller 'awrah means the genitals; the larger 'awrah in salah for men is from navel to knee.
2
Note the two opinions and their rationales
Two opinions are presented: (1) cover the back because it is more shameful during ruku' and sujud; (2) cover the front because it faces the qibla and cannot be covered by anything else, while the back is partially covered by the buttocks.
Both opinions rely on the principle of covering the more exposed or shameful part first.
3
Understand the proofs from Hanafi texts
The passage references al-Mubtagha: if one has cloth but does not cover, prayer is invalid. And Fath al-Qadir: if one finds something to cover part, it is obligatory to use it and cover both. These establish the baseline obligation.
These texts form the basis for the two opinions in the present case.
4
Recognize the validity of both opinions
The text does not give preference to either opinion; both are transmitted within the school. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) may lean toward covering the front due to the additional reasons of facing qibla and lack of natural coverage.
The ikhtilaf is a legitimate difference of opinion within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المبتغى بالمعجمة : وإن كان عنده قطعة يستر بها أصغر العورات فلم يستر فسدت وإلا فلا. وفي فتح القدير : ولو وجد ما يستر بعض العورة يجب استعماله ويستر القبل والدبر ا هـ . فإن لم يجد ما يستر به إلا أحدهما قيل يستر الدبر لأنه أفحش في حالة الركوع والسجود، وقيل يستر القبل لأنه يستقبل به القبلة ولأنه لا يستر بغيره والدبر يستر بالأليتين ا.هـ. كذا في السراج الوهاج.
And in al-Mubtagha (with a 'jim'): If he has a piece of cloth with which he can cover the smaller private parts and he does not cover, his prayer is invalid, otherwise not. And in Fath al-Qadir: If he finds something to cover some of the private parts, he must use it and cover the front and back. End quote. Then if he does not find anything to cover except one of them, it is said he covers the back because it is more shameful in the state of bowing and prostration; and it is said he covers the front because he faces the qibla with it and because it cannot be covered by anything else, while the back can be covered by the buttocks. End quote. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage presents two opinions on what a naked person should cover if he only has cloth for one of the two parts of the 'awrah (the front or back). The first opinion, which the text presents as one view, is that he should cover the back (dubur) because during ruku' and sujud, the back is more exposed and more shameful. The second opinion says he should cover the front (qubul) because he faces the qibla with it and the front has no natural covering like the buttocks cover the back somewhat. The text also cites a ruling from al-Mubtagha that if one has a cloth to cover only the 'smaller private parts' (the genitals), he must cover them, otherwise the prayer is invalid. And from Fath al-Qadir, if one has cloth to cover some of the 'awrah, he must use it and cover the front and back (both). The discussion reflects the Hanafi principles of prioritizing covering what is more exposed and shameful.

Key Terms
قبل (qubul): The front private part: the genitals.
دبر (dubur): The back private part: the anus.
أصغر العورات (asghar al-'awrat): The smaller private parts, i.e., the genitals (as opposed to the entire 'awrah from navel to knee).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to one of the opinions cited in the text, why should the back (dubur) be covered if only one part can be covered?
A) Because it is more shameful during ruku' and sujud
B) Because it faces the qibla
C) Because it cannot be covered by the buttocks
D) Because the front is smaller

Key Takeaway
When cloth is insufficient, the Hanafi school offers two priority rules; the mufta bihi is to cover the front due to qibla direction and natural cover of the back.

Congregational Prayer for the Naked and Repetition Obligation
Rulings on naked persons praying and repetition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on congregational prayer for naked persons and explain the condition under which repeating the prayer becomes wajib after finding clothing.

Core Idea
A naked person must repeat the prayer only if prevented by others; natural inability excuses.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses two related scenarios: a group of naked people praying together, and an individual who prayed naked later finding clothing. While congregational prayer for the naked is valid but disliked, the more critical question is whether the prayer must be repeated when covering becomes available. The Hanafi school distinguishes based on the cause of the inability to cover.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
First, note the ruling on congregational prayer: it is makruh but valid with conditions (distance, imam position, lowered gazes). Second, identify the ruling on repetition: wajib only when inability to cover was due to human prevention.
The passage uses 'إعادة' for repetition and 'منع من العباد' for prevention by people.
2
Locate the condition for repetition
The text explicitly links the obligation to repeat to 'if the inability was due to prevention from people, such as if his garment was taken from him.' This is the key condition (shart) that triggers wajib.
Contrast with natural inability (e.g., no cloth available) where no repetition is needed.
3
Understand the dalil (qiyas)
The Hanafi ruling is based on qiyas to tayammum: if a person is prevented from using water by another, they must repeat the prayer when water becomes available. Similarly, being prevented from covering by another triggers repetition.
This is a 'dalil aqli' (rational proof) analogizing two purification-related obligations.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Al-Nawawi reported a consensus that no repetition is required when praying out of inability. The Hanafi school restricts this consensus to natural inability, adding the exception for human prevention. The Shafi'i school does not make this distinction.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf where the Hanafi view is mufta bihi.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author of Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a later Hanafi authority, affirms the position that repetition is wajib under human prevention, indicating this is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view.
Authority weight: fatawa mutakhkhirin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسيأتي في باب الإمامة أن العراة لا يصلون جماعة. وفي الذخيرة وأستر ما يكون أن يتباعد بعضهم عن بعضهم إذا أمنوا العدو والسبع وإن صلوا جماعة صحت مع الكراهة. ويقف الإمام وسطهم وإن تقدم جاز، ويغضون أبصارهم سوى الإمام. ثم المصنف رحمه يذكر أن على العاري الإعادة إذا وجد ثوباً وقد أفاد النووي رحمه الله في شرح المهذب أنه لا خلاف بين المسلمين أنه لا تجب عليه الإعادة إذا صلى عارياً للعجز عن السترة ا هـ . أن تلزمه الإعادة عندنا إذا كان العجز لمنع من العباد كما إذا غصب ثوبه.
And it will come in the chapter on Imamate that naked persons do not pray in congregation. And in al-Dhakhira: The most concealing is that they distance themselves from each other if they are safe from enemy and beast, and if they pray in congregation it is valid with dislike. And the Imam stands in the middle of them, and if he is ahead, it is permissible, and they lower their gazes except the Imam. Then the author (may Allah have mercy on him) mentions that the naked person must repeat if he finds a garment, and al-Nawawi (may Allah have mercy on him) in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab stated that there is no difference among Muslims that he is not obligated to repeat if he prayed naked due to inability to cover. End quote. That he must repeat according to us if the inability was due to prevention from people, such as if his garment was taken from him.
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage discusses two related issues: congregational prayer for a group of naked people, and the obligation to repeat the prayer after finding clothing. For the first, although naked persons should not pray together, if they do, the prayer is valid but disliked (makruh). They should stand apart, and the Imam stands in the middle. For the second, the author states that according to the Hanafi school, if a person prayed naked due to being prevented by others (e.g., someone took his clothes), he must repeat the prayer when he finds clothing. This is based on qiyas (analogy) to the case of tayammum: if one is prevented from using water, he must repeat his prayer. Al-Nawawi's statement about consensus is general; the Hanafi position is an exception when the prevention is from human action.

Key Terms
إعادة (i'ada): Repeating the prayer after finding clothing when the previous prayer was performed without covering due to external prevention.
منع من العباد (man' min al-'ibad): Prevention by another person (e.g., someone seizing the garment).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in the text, when must a naked person repeat his prayer after finding clothing?
A) Always, regardless of the reason
B) Only if the inability to cover was due to being prevented by another person
C) Never, because the prayer was valid
D) Only if he prays in congregation

Key Takeaway
A naked person must repeat the prayer only when the inability to cover was caused by another person; natural inability does not require repetition.

Intention (Niyyah) as a Condition of Prayer
Discussion on the necessity, proof, and components of intention in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on intention in prayer, identify the primary proof (ijma), and explain why other proofs are insufficient.

Core Idea
Intention is a condition of prayer established by ijma, not by the hadith of intentions.

Intention (niyyah) is foundational for every act of worship. This passage from Bahr al-Raiq clarifies its ruling in prayer, explaining why the Hanafi school relies on consensus (ijma) rather than the well-known hadith. We will explore the definition of intention, the necessity of a single sincere intention, and the requirement that no foreign act intervene between intention and the opening takbir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its primary proof
Locate the author's statement that intention is a condition of prayer due to Islamic consensus (ijma). Note that he cites Ibn al-Mundhir's transmission. This is the core ruling.
Ijma is qat'i (certain) in both transmission and meaning, making the ruling fard (obligatory).
2
Understand why other proofs are rejected
The author dismisses the Quranic verse (al-Bayyina:5) because 'worship' there refers to tawhid, not prayer specifically. He also dismisses the hadith 'innama al-a'mal bi-nniyyat' because it is ahad (single transmission) and ambiguous, thus only indicating sunnah, not obligation.
This illustrates the Hanafi usul principle that ahad hadith produce zanni knowledge, insufficient for establishing a fard ruling.
3
Grasp the definition of niyyah and the one-intention view
The author defines intention as 'desiring to pray to Allah with sincerity'. He refutes the claim that three intentions are needed (prayer, sincerity, qibla), stating that one intention suffices because sincerity is inherent. Facing the qibla is not a separate condition.
This simplifies practice: the worshipper only needs the intention to perform the specific prayer sincerely for Allah.
4
Learn the condition of no foreign act
The phrase 'without a foreign act' means that between intention and takbir there should be no action incompatible with prayer, such as eating, drinking, or speaking. Walking and wudu' are not foreign acts and do not invalidate the intention.
This protects the continuity of intention; the worshipper may walk or perform wudu' after intending as long as he does not engage in extraneous worldly acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والنية بلا فاصل) يعني من شروط الصلاة لإجماع المسلمين على ذلك كما نقله ابن المنذر وغيره. وأما الاستدلال على اشتراطها بقوله تعالى وما أمروا إلا ليعبدوا الله مخلصين له الدين) [البينة : ٥] كما فعله السراج الهندي في شرح المغني فليس بظاهر لأن الظاهر أن العبادة بمعنى التوحيد بدليل عطف الصلاة والزكاة عليها، وأما الاستدلال بقوله «إنما الأعمال بالنيات كما في الهداية وغيرها فلا يصح لأن الأصوليين ذكروا أن الحديث من قبيل ظني الثبوت والدلالة لأنه خبر واحد مشترك الدلالة فيفيد السنية والاستحباب لا الافتراض، والنية إرادة الصلاة الله تعالى على الخلوص وقد قدمنا في الوضوء الكلام عليها. وقول الشارح أن المصلي يحتاج إلى ثلاث نيات نية الصلاة التي يدخل فيها، ونية الاخلاص الله تعالى ونية استقبال القبلة فيه نظر؛ بل المحتاج إليه نية واحدة وهي ما ذكرناه. فقولنا على الخلوص يغني عن الثانية. وأما نية استقبال القبلة فليست شرطاً على الصحيح كما ذكره في المبسوط، سواء كان يصلي إلى المحراب أو في الصحراء، والمراد بقوله بلا فاصل أي بين النية والتكبير الفاصل الأجنبي وهو عمل لا يليق في الصلاة كالأكل والشرب لأن هذه الأفعال تبطل الصلاة فتبطل النية وشراء الحطب والكلام، وأما المشي والوضوء فليس بأجنبي، ألا ترى أن من أحدث في صلاته له أن يفعل ذلك ولا يمنعه من المسألة. ولا بعذر كما سبق جرى فيها التفصيل لأهميتها بخلاف ستر العورة فإنه يسقط بالعذر كما ترى فليتأمل اهـ.
His statement: (and intention without a foreign act) means it is a condition of prayer due to the consensus of the Muslims on that, as transmitted by Ibn al-Mundhir and others. As for proving its conditionality by His statement (And they were not commanded except to worship Allah, being sincere to Him in religion) [al-Bayyina:5], as done by al-Siraj al-Hindi in Sharh al-Mughni, it is not apparent because the apparent meaning is that 'worship' means tawhid, evidenced by the conjunction of prayer and zakat with it. And as for the proof by his saying (Indeed, actions are by intentions) as in al-Hidayah and others, it is not valid because the usul scholars mentioned that the hadith is of the type of zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala because it is ahad and ambiguous in meaning, so it indicates sunnah and recommendation, not obligation. And intention is the desire to pray to Allah with sincerity, and we have already spoken about it in wudu'. And the statement of the commentator that the praying person needs three intentions: intention of the prayer he enters, intention of sincerity to Allah, and intention of facing the qibla, is questionable; rather what is needed is one intention, which is what we have mentioned. So our saying 'with sincerity' suffices for the second. And as for the intention of facing the qibla, it is not a condition according to the correct view, as mentioned in al-Mabsut, whether he prays in a mihrab or in the desert. And the meaning of his saying 'without a foreign act' is that between the intention and the takbir there is no foreign intervening act, which is an action not befitting the prayer, such as eating and drinking, because these actions invalidate the prayer and thus invalidate the intention, and also buying firewood and speaking. As for walking and wudu', they are not foreign; do you not see that the one who has an event in his prayer may do that and it does not prevent him? And without excuse as previously discussed in detail due to its importance, unlike covering the 'awrah which drops due to excuse, as you see, so ponder. End quote.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage clarifies the ruling of intention (niyyah) as a condition of prayer. The author states that it is established by consensus (ijma), not by the Quranic verse (al-Bayyina 5) because 'worship' there means tawhid, and not by the hadith 'innama al-a'mal bi-nniyyat' because the hadith is ahad (single transmission) and ambiguous in meaning, so it only indicates sunnah, not obligation. He defines intention as 'desiring to pray to Allah with sincerity'. He then refutes the claim that three intentions are required (prayer, sincerity, qibla), stating that only one intention is needed: to pray with sincerity, which encompasses sincerity. Facing the qibla is not a separate condition for intention. Finally, he explains the phrase 'without a foreign act' (bila fasil): between intention and takbir, there should be no extraneous act that is incompatible with prayer, like eating, drinking, or buying firewood. Walking or performing wudu' are not considered foreign.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): The intention to pray with sincerity; it is a condition of prayer established by consensus.
فاصل أجنبي (fasil ajnabi): A foreign act between intention and takbir that is incompatible with prayer, invalidating the intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the primary proof that intention is a condition of prayer?
A) The Quranic verse 'They were not commanded except to worship Allah'
B) The hadith 'Indeed, actions are by intentions'
C) The consensus (ijma) of the Muslims
D) The practice of the Companions

Key Takeaway
Intention (niyyah) is a condition of prayer established by consensus, not by the hadith, and it must be free from foreign acts between intention and takbir.

Timing of Niyyah: Advancing Intention Before Takbir
Discussion on permissibility of advancing niyyah before takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the timing of niyyah for prayer and explain why simultaneity is not required, citing the dalil and the principle of removing hardship.

Core Idea
The intention can precede the takbir — hardship is removed, and the absolute text is followed.

When you stand for prayer, you must have intention (niyyah) to distinguish worship from habit. But must that intention be exactly at the moment of saying Allahu Akbar, or can it come a little earlier? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq unpacks the Hanafi ruling, which allows advancing the intention after the time enters, provided no foreign act intervenes. By understanding this, you learn how the Hanafi school balances textual evidence with the removal of hardship, and why this differs from the Shafi'i requirement of simultaneity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
What exactly is being disputed? The timing of the intention (niyyah) for prayer: must it be simultaneous with the opening takbir, or can it precede it?
The dispute is both intra-Hanafi (between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad) and inter-madhhab (between Hanafi and Shafi'i).
2
State the Hanafi position
What does the Hanafi school hold as the relied-upon view? Intention may be made before the takbir after the time of the prayer has entered, as long as no foreign act intervenes.
The zahir al-riwayah position is from the six core books of Imam Muhammad.
3
Identify the opposing view and its dalil
Imam al-Shafi'i requires the intention to be exactly simultaneous with the commencement of the prayer, because sincerity (ikhlas) is realized at the start of the act.
This view is also held by al-Tahawi but as a recommended precaution, not a condition.
4
Analyze the Hanafi dalil and response
The Hanafi school relies on the absolute wording of the hadith 'Innama li kull imri'in ma nawa' and the principle that requiring exact simultaneity causes hardship (haraj) and leads to obsessive whispers (waswasa). The text is absolute and cannot be restricted without evidence.
Analogy is drawn to fasting, zakat, and hajj where intention may precede the action.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In practice, a Hanafi may intend the prayer a moment before saying Allahu Akbar, while a Shafi'i must consciously renew the intention exactly with the takbir.
This difference eases the burden on the worshipper and prevents waswasa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البناء . وبهذا علم أن الصلاة تجوز بنية متقدمة على الشروط إذا لم يفصل أجنبي كما صرحوا به، فظاهر إطلاقهم يفيد أن النية قبل دخول الوقت صحيحة كالطهارة قبله لكن ذكر ابن أمير حاج عن ابن هبيرة اشتراط دخول الوقت للنية المتقدمة عن أبي حنيفة وهو مشكل وفي ثبوته تردد لا يخفى لعدم وجوده في كتب المذهب وفي الظهيرية وعند محمد يجوز تقديم النية في العبادات : هو الصحيح، وعند أبي يوسف لا يجوز إلا في الصوم ا اهـ. وفي منية المصلي والأحوط أن ينوي مقارناً للتكبير ومخالطاً له كما هو مذهب الشافعي ا هـ. وبه قال الطحاوي لكن عندنا هذا الاحتياط مستحب وليس بشرط ، وعند الشافعي شرط لأن الحاجة إلى النية لتحقق معنى الاخلاص وذلك عند الشروع لا قبله قلنا النص مطلق فلا يجوز تخصيصه بالرأي على أن قوله وإنما لكل امرئ ما نوى يفيد أنه يكون له ما نوى إذا تقدمت النية، فالقول بأنه لا يكون له ما نوى خلاف النص، ولأن اشتراط القرآن لا يخلو عن الحرج مع ما في التزامه من فتح باب الوسواس فلا يشترط كما في الصوم والزكاة والحج، حتى لو خرج من بيته يريد الحج فأحرم ولم تحضره النية جاز. ثم فسر النووي القرآن بأن يأتي بالنية مع أوّل التكبير ويستصحبها إلى آخره، وذكر في شرح المهذب أنه لا يجب التدقيق في تحقيق المقارنة وأنه يكفي المقارنة العرفية في ذلك بحيث يعد مستحضراً لصلاته غير غافل عنها اقتداء بالسلف الصالحين في مسامحتهم في ذلك. وأشار المصنف إلى أنها لا تجوز بنية متأخرة خلافاً للكرخي قياساً على الصوم وهو فاسد، لأن سقوط القران لمكان الحرج والحرج يندفع بتقديم النية فلا ضرورة إلى التأخير، وجوز التأخير في الصوم للحرج. وبهذا علم أن ما في خزانة الفتاوى والعتابي «نسي النية فنوى عند قوله «ولا إله غيرك يصير شارعاً مبني على قول الكرخي على تخريج بعض المشايخ أنه يجوز إلى انتهاء الثناء، وقيل إلى أن يركع وهو مروي عن محمد. كذا في المجتبى . وقيل إلى أن يرفع رأسه من الركوع، وقيل إلى التعوّذ وفي البدائع : لو نوى بعد قوله « الله» قبل أكبر» لا يجوز لأن الشروع يصح معطوف على الأكل والشرب والأولى ذكره عقبه كما يوجد في بعض النسخ. قوله : (لعدم وجوده في كتب المذهب) قال الشيخ اسماعيل : قد وجدت المسألة والله الحمد في مجموع المسائل وهو من كتب المذهب. واختلفوا في النية هل يجوز تقديمها على التكبير أو تكون مقارنة له فقال أبو حنيفة وأحمد رحمهم الله : يجوز تقديم النية للصلاة بعد دخول الوقت وقبل التكبير ما لم يقطع بعمل اهـ. وفي الجواهر وابن صُبر بضم الصاد. محمد بن عبد الرحمن بن صبر القاضي البغدادي الفقيه، ولد سنة عشرين وثلثمائة وتوفي سنة ثمانين وثلثمائة .اهـ. فما في النهر من أنه أبو صبرة ليس بصواب اهـ. وما في نسخ البحر من قوله ابن هبيرة هو الذي رأيته في شرح المنية لابن أمير حاج. قوله : (وهو فاسد الخ) بهذا يعلم ما في قول الدرر بعد نقله الأقوال الآتية وفائدة هذه الروايات أن المصلي إذا
The building [of the prayer]. And by this it is known that prayer is valid with an intention advanced before the conditions if no foreign act intervenes, as they have explicitly stated. So the apparent meaning of their general statements indicates that the intention before the time [of prayer] is valid like purification before it. However, Ibn Amir Haj mentioned from Ibn Hubayra the condition of the entry of time for the advanced intention from Abu Hanifa, and this is problematic, and there is hesitation in its establishment, not hidden, due to its absence in the books of the school. And in al-Zahiriyya: According to Muhammad, advancing the intention in acts of worship is permissible; that is the correct view. According to Abu Yusuf, it is not permissible except in fasting. And in Munyat al-Musalli: The most precautionary is that one intends simultaneously with the takbir and mixing with it, as is the school of al-Shafi'i. And al-Tahawi said the same. But in our [Hanafi] view, this precaution is recommended and not a condition. According to al-Shafi'i, it is a condition because the need for intention is to realize the meaning of sincerity, and that is at the commencement [of the act], not before it. We say: The text [hadith] is absolute, so it is not permissible to restrict it by opinion. Moreover, his statement 'And for each person is what he intended' indicates that he gets what he intended if the intention preceded. So the statement that he does not get what he intended contradicts the text. And because requiring simultaneity involves hardship and opens the door to waswasa (whisperings), so it is not required as in fasting, zakat, and hajj. Even if someone left his house intending hajj and performed ihram without the intention being present [consciously], it is valid. Then al-Nawawi interpreted 'simultaneity' as bringing the intention with the beginning of the takbir and maintaining it until the end. And in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab it is mentioned that one does not have to be precise in achieving simultaneity; rather, customary simultaneity suffices such that he is considered present-minded about his prayer, not heedless of it, following the righteous predecessors in their leniency in that. The author [of Kanz al-Daqa'iq] indicated that it is not valid with a delayed intention, contrary to al-Karkhi, by analogy with fasting, and this is invalid because the dropping of simultaneity is due to hardship, and hardship is alleviated by advancing the intention, so there is no need for delay. Delay is permitted in fasting due to hardship. And by this it is known that what is in Khizanat al-Fatawa and al-Atabi: 'He forgot the intention and intended at his saying 'La ilaha ghayruk' — he becomes a starter' is based on the statement of al-Karkhi, according to the derivation of some shaykhs that it is permissible until the end of the thana', and it is said until he bows, and that is narrated from Muhammad. Similarly, in al-Mujtaba. And it is said until he raises his head from bowing, and it is said until al-Ta'awwudh. In al-Bada'i: If he intended after saying 'Allah' before 'Akbar', it is not valid because the commencement is considered connected to eating and drinking, and it is better to mention it after it as is found in some copies. His statement: (Due to its non-existence in the books of the school) — Shaykh Ismail said: I have found the issue, praise be to Allah, in Majmu' al-Masa'il, which is from the books of the school. And they differed concerning the intention: Is it permissible to advance it before the takbir or must it be simultaneous? Abu Hanifa and Ahmad (may Allah have mercy on them) said: It is permissible to advance the intention for prayer after the entry of time and before the takbir, as long as he does not cut it by an action. And in al-Jawahir and Ibn Subr (with dammah on the sad): Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn Subr, the judge of Baghdad, the jurist, born in 320 AH and died in 380 AH. So what is in al-Nahr that he is Abu Sabra is not correct. And what is in copies of al-Bahr from his statement Ibn Hubayra is what I saw in Sharh al-Munya by Ibn Amir Haj. His statement: (And it is invalid, etc.) — By this it is known what is in the statement of al-Durar after quoting the following sayings: 'The benefit of these narrations is that the person praying if...'
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses a key dispute in the Hanafi school and between madhhabs regarding the timing of the intention (niyyah) for prayer. The author begins by stating that prayer is valid with an intention made before the conditions (like purification) if there is no foreign intervening act. He then examines the question of whether the intention must be simultaneous with the takbir or can precede it. The Hanafi position, attributed to Abu Hanifa and Imam Ahmad, permits advancing the intention after the time has entered, as long as one does not interrupt it with a significant action. Imam Muhammad holds that advancing intention is generally permissible; Abu Yusuf restricts it to fasting. The Shafi'i school requires simultaneity, citing the need for sincerity at the very start of the act. The Hanafi response relies on the absolute wording of the hadith 'Verily actions are by intentions, and for every person is what he intended,' arguing that if intention precedes, one still gets the intended reward. Requiring exact simultaneity would cause hardship and open the door to obsessive whispers (waswasa), so it is not a condition, analogously to fasting, zakat, and hajj. The commentator also addresses later views, like al-Karkhi's allowance of a delayed intention (up to certain points in the prayer), which is rejected by the author as invalid because there is no need for delay when advance intention is sufficient. The passage concludes with a biographical note about a certain Ibn Subr, correcting a mistaken identification. Overall, the Hanafi position is that the intention can be made before the takbir, provided it is not separated by a foreign act, and that simultaneous intention is recommended but not obligatory.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): The intention that distinguishes an act of worship from a habit; it is an act of the heart, not the tongue.
تكبير (takbir): The opening phrase 'Allahu Akbar' that commences the prayer (tahrimah).
مقارنة (muqaranah): The simultaneity of intention with the action, which is required by some but not by the Hanafis.
حرج (haraj): Hardship or difficulty that justifies leniency in the law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is it permissible to make the intention for the Zuhr prayer?
A) Only at the moment of saying 'Allahu Akbar'
B) Any time before the prayer, even before the time enters
C) After the time of Zuhr has entered, before the takbir, as long as no foreign act intervenes
D) Only during the first rak'ah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits advancing the intention before the takbir, relying on the absolute hadith and the principle of removing hardship, making it easy for worshippers.

Prior Intention Suffices for Prayer
States the madhhab ruling that prior intention suffices for validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that prior intention suffices for prayer, explain the condition of no intervening unrelated act, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i and the stricter view within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Prior intention suffices; contemporaneity not required.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on intention (niyyah) in prayer. The key question is: must one consciously recall the intention at the moment of takbir, or does an earlier intention suffice? The passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that the madhhab accepts a prior intention as long as no contradictory act intervenes. This ruling is supported by Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and although Muhammad ibn al-Hasan held a stricter view, the relied-upon position follows the majority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is intention (niyyah) for prayer. The Hanafi ruling is that the prayer is valid (sahih) with a prior intention, even if not recalled at takbir.
2
Determine the condition for validity
The prior intention must be for a specific prayer, and no act unrelated to prayer must intervene between the intention and the start of prayer.
e.g., leaving the house with the intention to pray, then going directly to the mosque.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad initially required the intention to be present at takbir and throughout, but later narrations allow prior intention. His stricter view: if one needs to reflect to answer 'what prayer?', the prayer is invalid.
The majority and mufta bihi follow the lenient view.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Shafi'i school requires muqarana (intention simultaneous with takbir). The Hanafi school does not require this, considering it sunnah rather than fard.
This is a key practical difference.
5
Apply to a scenario
If a person intended zuhr during wudu, walked to the mosque without worldly engagement, and said takbir without recalling the intention, the prayer is valid according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
This scenario is directly from the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإلا فالمذهب أنها تجوز بنية متقدمة على الشروع بشرطه المتقدم، سواء كان بحيث يقدر على الجواب من غير تفكر أو لا، ولهذا قال في الخانية والخلاصة : ولو نوى قبل الشروع ؛ فعن محمد أنه لو نوى عند الوضوء أن يصلي الظهر أو العصر مع الإمام ولم يشتغل بعد النية بما ليس من جنس الصلاة إلا أنه لما انتهى إلى مكان الصلاة لم تحضره النية جازت صلاته بتلك النية وهكذا روي عن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، وفي البدائع. وقد روي عن أبي يوسف فيمن خرج من منزله يريد الفرض في الجماعة فلما انتهى إلى الإمام كبر ولم تحضره النية في تلك الساعة أنه يجوز . قال الكرخي : ولا أعلم أن أحداً من علمائنا خالف أبا يوسف في ذلك ا.هـ. وهو يفيد أنه يكفي تقدم أصل النية. ونية التعيين للفرائض ولا يشترط المقارنة ولا الاستحضار لما نواه في أثنائها، بل كلام محمد بن يقتضي أنه لا يكفي مقارنة النية للتكبير بل لا بد من الاستحضار لها إلى آخر الصلاة لأنه قال : لو احتاج إلى تفكر بعد السؤال لا تصح صلاته
Otherwise, the madhhab is that it is permissible with a prior intention before commencing, with its prior condition, whether he is able to answer without reflection or not. For this reason it is stated in al-Khaniyah and al-Khulasah: If one intended before commencing; from Muhammad: if he intended at the time of wudu to pray zuhr or asr with the imam, and he did not engage after the intention in something not of the category of prayer, but when he reached the place of prayer the intention did not occur to him, his prayer is valid with that intention. This is also narrated from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. In al-Bada'i: It is narrated from Abu Yusuf regarding someone who left his home intending the obligatory prayer in congregation, when he reached the imam he said the takbir and the intention did not occur to him at that moment, that it is permissible. Al-Karkhi said: I do not know any of our scholars who opposed Abu Yusuf in this. End quote. This indicates that the prior essence of intention suffices, and the intention of specification for obligatory prayers, and contemporaneity (muqarana) is not required, nor is keeping the intention present throughout. Rather, the statement of Muhammad implies that contemporaneity of the intention with the takbir is not sufficient, but rather it must be present until the end of the prayer, because he said: If he needed to reflect after being asked, his prayer is not valid.
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a prior intention (niyyah mutaqaddimah). The madhhab holds that if one forms the intention before entering the prayer, e.g., when making wudu or leaving home, and does nothing to break that intention (like engaging in worldly affairs), then even if he does not recall the intention at the moment of takbir, his prayer is valid. This is based on narrations from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan. Abu Yusuf’s view is that it suffices, and al-Karkhi notes consensus among Hanafi scholars on this. The passage distinguishes between the essence of intention (asl al-niyyah) and keeping it present (istihdar). Contemporaneity (muqarana) is not a condition; a prior intention suffices. However, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan holds a stricter view: if one would need to think to answer what prayer he is doing, the intention is not valid, implying he requires constant awareness. But the madhhab follows the more lenient view that prior intention suffices.

Key Terms
النية المتقدمة (al-niyyah al-mutaqaddimah): An intention formed before the commencement of the prayer, which remains valid even if not consciously recalled at the moment of takbir.
المقارنة (al-muqārana): The contemporaneity of intention with the opening takbir. Hanafi does not require this.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the condition for a prior intention (niyyah mutaqaddimah) to be valid for prayer?
A) The intention must be recalled at the moment of takbir.
B) The intention must be made immediately before takbir.
C) The intention must not be followed by any act unrelated to prayer.
D) The intention must be repeated during the prayer.

Key Takeaway
A prior intention for prayer is valid in the Hanafi school provided no worldly act intervenes between the intention and the start of prayer.

Ruling on Vocalizing Intention (Niyyah)
Discusses Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on vocalizing intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on vocalizing intention and explain why it is not required, and critique the false attribution to Imam al-Shafi'i that it is necessary.

Core Idea
Intention is an act of the heart; vocalizing it is a help, not a requirement.

This lesson examines the legal status of vocalizing the intention (talfuz bil-niyyah) before prayer. While many Muslims are accustomed to uttering their intention aloud, the classical Hanafi position—and indeed the consensus of the four schools—is that intention is purely an act of the heart. The passage clarifies a common misunderstanding about Imam al-Shafi'i's view and addresses internal Hanafi differences on whether vocalization is sunnah, mustahab, or even bid'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and its relevance
Recognize that the debate concerns whether saying 'I intend to pray such-and-such' is required for the validity of prayer. The text clarifies that this vocalization is not a condition (shart).
The issue is often discussed under the conditions of prayer.
2
Survey the intra-Hanafi opinions
Note the range of Hanafi positions: from sunnah (Muhammad al-Shaybani) to mustahab (Munya) to bid'ah (Fath al-Qadir) except when needed for concentration.
The Zahir al-Riwayah position (Muhammad) is that it is sunnah.
3
Examine the claimed Shafi'i position
The author refutes the claim that Imam al-Shafi'i required vocalization. Actually, Shafi'is consider it sunnah, not wajib. The attribution is false.
Consensus among all four imams: vocalization is not obligatory.
4
Analyze the primary dalil
The Hanafi proof: No authentic hadith reports the Prophet (peace be upon him) or his Companions vocalizing the intention; they only said the takbir.
This dalil is used to argue that vocalization is not part of the established sunnah.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view is that intention is by the heart alone; vocalization is not required but may be done if it aids concentration, without believing it is necessary.
Al-Haskafi's emphasis on the heart-based intention is preferred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد اختلف كلام المشايخ في التلفظ باللسان فذكر في منية المصلي أنه مستحب وهو المختار وصححه في المجتبى. وفي الهداية والكافي والتبيين أنه يحسن لاجتماع عزيمته، وفي الاختيار معزياً إلى محمد بن الحسن أن سنة، وهكذا في المحيط والبدائع. وفي القنية : إنه بدعة إلا أن لا يمكنه إقامتها في القلب إلا بإجرائها على اللسان فحينئذ يباح . ونقل عن بعضهم أن السنة الاقتصار على نية القلب فإن عبر عنه بلسانه جاز. ونقل في شرح المنية عن بعضهم الكراهة وطاهر ما في فتح القدير اختيار أنه بدعة فإنه قال قال بعض الحفاظ : لم يثبت عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من طريق صحيح ولا ضعيف أنه كان يقول عند الافتتاح أصلي كذا ولا عن أحد من الصحابة والتابعين بل المنقول أنه كان إذا قام إلى الصلاة كبر وهذه بدعة ا هـ. وقد يفهم من قول المصنف الاجتماع عزيمته أنه لا يحسن لغير هذا القصد وهذا لأن الإنسان قد يغلب عليه تفرق خاطره فإذا ذكر بلسانه كان عوناً على جمعه . ثم رأيته في التنجيس قال : والنية بالقلب لأنه عمله والتكلم لا معتبر به، ومن اختاره الحصكفي حيث قال : وهو أي عمل القلب أن يعلم عند الإرادة بداهة بلا تأمل أي صلاة يصلي حيث قيد بقوله «عند الإرادة دفعاً لما توهمه صاحب البحر . قوله : (وعند الشافعي رحمه الله لا بد من الذكر باللسان) فإنه ليس هذا مذهب الشافعي بل الذي ذكره الشافعية أنه سنة، وسيأتي عن شرح المنية أنه لم ينقل عن الأئمة الأربعة وفي شرح الشيخ اسمعيل سبق عن العيون وصرح به غير واحد أنه لا يشترط الذكر باللسان بالإجماع، فما في الخانية والنهاية ومجموع المسائل والمفتاح وغيرها. أنه من
And the statements of the scholars have differed regarding vocalization with the tongue. It is mentioned in Munyat al-Musalli that it is mustahab (recommended), and it is the chosen view, and it was declared correct in al-Mujtaba. In al-Hidayah, al-Kafi, and al-Tabyin, it is said to be good (yahsun) for gathering one's resolve. In al-Ikhtiyar, attributed to Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, it is sunnah. Similarly in al-Muhit and al-Bada'i. In al-Qunyah: it is bid'ah (innovation) unless he cannot establish it in his heart except by uttering it on his tongue, then it is permissible. It is transmitted from some that the sunnah is to confine to the heart intention, and if he expresses it with his tongue it is permissible. It is transmitted in Sharh al-Munya from some that it is disliked (karahah). The clear statement in Fath al-Qadir is the choice that it is bid'ah, for he said: Some memorizers said: It is not confirmed from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) by any authentic or weak chain that he would say upon opening 'I pray such and such', nor from any of the Companions or Successors. Rather, it is transmitted that when he stood for prayer he said the takbir. This is bid'ah. End quote. It may be understood from the author's statement 'gathering his resolve' that it is good for no other purpose, because one may be overcome by distraction, so if he mentions with his tongue it helps gather his mind. Then I saw in al-Tanjis he said: intention is by the heart because it is its action, and speech is not considered. And al-Haskafi chose this, where he said: it is the act of the heart that he knows at the time of willing spontaneously without reflection which prayer he is praying, as he qualified with 'at the time of willing' to rebut what the author of al-Bahr imagined. His statement: (And according to al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, remembrance with the tongue is necessary) — then this is not the madhhab of al-Shafi'i. Rather, what the Shafi'is mention is that it is sunnah. And it will come in Sharh al-Munya that it is not transmitted from the four imams. And in the commentary of Shaykh Isma'il, it preceded from al-Uyun, and more than one declared that remembrance with the tongue is not required by consensus. Thus what is in al-Khaniyah, al-Nihayah, Majmu' al-Masa'il, al-Miftah, and others, that it is…
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage addresses a debated issue within the Hanafi school: should one vocalize the intention (niyyah) before prayer? The text surveys several positions: some Hanafi scholars consider it mustahab (recommended), some consider it sunnah, and others deem it bid'ah (innovation), except when one cannot concentrate otherwise. The author then critiques a claim attributed to Imam al-Shafi'i that vocalization is necessary. The text clarifies that this is not the Shafi'i position; rather, Shafi'is consider it sunnah. The consensus among the four schools, as stated, is that vocalization is not required. The passage emphasizes that intention is an act of the heart (al-niyyah bi al-qalb), and verbal expression is not a condition. This is the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Key Terms
التلفظ بالنية (al-talfuz bil-niyyah): Verbally expressing one's intention before prayer, e.g., saying 'I intend to pray Zuhr.'
النية بالقلب (al-niyyah bil-qalb): The intention formed in the heart, which is the essential and valid intention.

Key Takeaway
Vocalizing the intention is not a condition for prayer; intention is solely an act of the heart, and this is agreed upon by all four imams.

Prior Niyyah: Permissible Without Concurrency
A discussion of the timing of niyyah in prayer and the intra-Hanafi difference on prior niyyah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that niyyah may precede takbir and distinguish the intra-Hanafi views on prior niyyah.

Core Idea
Niyyah before takbir is valid; muqaranah is not a condition.

In determining the validity of prayer, the timing of niyyah (intention) is crucial. This lesson examines whether the niyyah must be concurrent with the opening takbir (muqaranah) or can be established earlier. The Hanafi school adopts a lenient stance, allowing prior niyyah, but there are subtle differences among its early authorities that shape the relied-upon fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central issue
Determine whether simultaneity of niyyah with takbir is required or if prior niyyah suffices.
The passage contrasts prior niyyah with muqaranah.
2
State the general Hanafi ruling
Prior niyyah suffices as long as no act foreign to prayer intervenes between niyyah and takbir.
This is the majority position from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Compare the positions: Muhammad ibn Salamah (and some riwayat from Imam Muhammad) require ability to answer without thinking; Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa permit even if thinking is needed.
Al-Karkhi's statement confirms no opposition to Abu Yusuf.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is Abu Yusuf's: prior niyyah suffices even if not present at takbir.
Al-Karkhi: 'I do not know anyone among our scholars who opposed Abu Yusuf.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من غير فكر وعزاه في منية المصلي إلى الأجناس فإنما هو قول محمد بن سلمة كما ذكره في البدائع والخانية والخلاصة وإلا فالمذهب أنها تجوز بنية متقدمة على الشروع بشرطه المتقدم، سواء كان بحيث يقدر على الجواب من غير تفكر أو لا، ولهذا قال في الخانية والخلاصة : ولو نوى قبل الشروع ؛ فعن محمد أنه لو نوى عند الوضوء أن يصلي الظهر أو العصر مع الإمام ولم يشتغل بعد النية بما ليس من جنس الصلاة إلا أنه لما انتهى إلى مكان الصلاة لم تحضره النية جازت صلاته بتلك النية وهكذا روي عن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، وفي البدائع. وقد روي عن أبي يوسف فيمن خرج من منزله يريد الفرض في الجماعة فلما انتهى إلى الإمام كبر ولم تحضره النية في تلك الساعة أنه يجوز . قال الكرخي : ولا أعلم أن أحداً من علمائنا خالف أبا يوسف في ذلك ا.هـ. وهو يفيد أنه يكفي تقدم أصل النية. ونية التعيين للفرائض ولا يشترط المقارنة ولا الاستحضار لما نواه في أثنائها، بل كلام محمد بن يقتضي أنه لا يكفي مقارنة النية للتكبير بل لا بد من الاستحضار لها إلى آخر الصلاة لأنه قال : لو احتاج إلى تفكر بعد السؤال لا تصح صلاته، وقد أجمع العلماء على أنه لو نوى بقلبه ولم يتكلم فإنه يجوز كما حكاه غير واحد فما في الخانية وعند الشافعي لا بد من الذكر باللسان مردود.
Without thought, and he attributed it in Munyat al-Musalli to al-Ajnas—it is only the saying of Muhammad ibn Salamah as mentioned in al-Bada'i', al-Khaniyah, and al-Khulasah. Otherwise, the madhhab is that it is permissible with a niyyah preceding the commencement with its prior condition, whether he is able to respond without thought or not. For this reason, it is said in al-Khaniyah and al-Khulasah: If one intends before commencing—from Muhammad that if he intended at the time of wudu to pray Zuhr or Asr with the imam and did not occupy himself after the niyyah with something not of the same type as prayer, but when he reached the place of prayer the niyyah did not occur to him, his prayer is valid with that niyyah. Similarly, it is narrated from Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf. In al-Bada'i': It is narrated from Abu Yusuf regarding one who left his house intending the obligatory prayer in congregation, and when he reached the imam he said takbir and the niyyah did not occur to him at that moment—that it is valid. Al-Karkhi said: I do not know anyone among our scholars who opposed Abu Yusuf in that. This indicates that the mere precedence of the original niyyah is sufficient, and the niyyah of specification for the obligatory prayers; simultaneity is not required, nor is keeping the intended prayer in mind during the prayer. Rather, the speech of Muhammad indicates that simultaneity of niyyah with takbir is not sufficient; rather, it is necessary to keep it in mind until the end of the prayer, because he said: If he needs to think after the query, his prayer is not valid. The scholars are unanimous that if one intends in his heart and does not speak, it is valid, as narrated by more than one. So what is in al-Khaniyah—'And according to al-Shafi'i, verbal mention is necessary'—is rejected.
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage deals with the timing of niyyah in prayer: must it be concurrent with the opening takbir, or can it precede? The author begins by attributing a position to 'Muhammad ibn Salamah' (a narrator of the madhhab) that prior niyyah requires that one be able to answer without thinking, but the author clarifies that the madhhab permits prior niyyah even if thinking is needed. Evidence is cited from Muhammad al-Shaybani, Abu Hanifah, and Abu Yusuf that a niyyah made at wudu for a specific prayer suffices even if one does not recall it at takbir, provided no act foreign to prayer intervenes. Abu Yusuf even permits prior intention without needing the niyyah to be present at takbir. Al-Karkhi notes no disagreement among Hanafis. The passage then refutes a report attributed to al-Shafi'i that verbal utterance is necessary, stating this is rejected.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intentional resolve in the heart to perform a specific act of worship.
مقارنة (muqaranah): The simultaneity of niyyah with the opening takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which Hanafi authority's position is relied upon regarding prior niyyah?
A) Muhammad ibn Salamah
B) Abu Yusuf
C) Abu Hanifah
D) Al-Shafi'i

Key Takeaway
Niyyah can precede takbir; concurrency is not a condition, and the position of Abu Yusuf is the relied-upon fatwa.
