Verbal Niyyah Not Required: Refuting a False Attribution
A refutation of the claim that verbal niyyah is required.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi ruling that verbal utterance of niyyah is not required and evaluate the refutation of the claim that al-Shafi'i requires it.

Core Idea
Intention in the heart suffices; verbal utterance is not mandatory by consensus.

A common point of confusion is whether the niyyah (intention) for prayer must be spoken aloud. Some have attributed to Imam al-Shafi'i the requirement of verbal mention. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position and shows that the attribution is rejected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
Recognize the attribution that al-Shafi'i requires verbal utterance of niyyah.
The passage in al-Khaniyah allegedly states this.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
Niyyah in the heart is sufficient; verbal utterance is not required, based on consensus.
The passage cites ijma' as evidence.
3
Evaluate the refutation
The text rejects the attribution as 'mardud' (rejected) and notes that it is not the actual Shafi'i position.
The real Shafi'i view considers verbal mention recommended, not obligatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من غير فكر وعزاه في منية المصلي إلى الأجناس فإنما هو قول محمد بن سلمة كما ذكره في البدائع والخانية والخلاصة وإلا فالمذهب أنها تجوز بنية متقدمة على الشروع بشرطه المتقدم، سواء كان بحيث يقدر على الجواب من غير تفكر أو لا، ولهذا قال في الخانية والخلاصة : ولو نوى قبل الشروع ؛ فعن محمد أنه لو نوى عند الوضوء أن يصلي الظهر أو العصر مع الإمام ولم يشتغل بعد النية بما ليس من جنس الصلاة إلا أنه لما انتهى إلى مكان الصلاة لم تحضره النية جازت صلاته بتلك النية وهكذا روي عن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، وفي البدائع. وقد روي عن أبي يوسف فيمن خرج من منزله يريد الفرض في الجماعة فلما انتهى إلى الإمام كبر ولم تحضره النية في تلك الساعة أنه يجوز . قال الكرخي : ولا أعلم أن أحداً من علمائنا خالف أبا يوسف في ذلك ا.هـ. وهو يفيد أنه يكفي تقدم أصل النية. ونية التعيين للفرائض ولا يشترط المقارنة ولا الاستحضار لما نواه في أثنائها، بل كلام محمد بن يقتضي أنه لا يكفي مقارنة النية للتكبير بل لا بد من الاستحضار لها إلى آخر الصلاة لأنه قال : لو احتاج إلى تفكر بعد السؤال لا تصح صلاته، وقد أجمع العلماء على أنه لو نوى بقلبه ولم يتكلم فإنه يجوز كما حكاه غير واحد فما في الخانية وعند الشافعي لا بد من الذكر باللسان مردود.
Without thought, and he attributed it in Munyat al-Musalli to al-Ajnas—it is only the saying of Muhammad ibn Salamah as mentioned in al-Bada'i', al-Khaniyah, and al-Khulasah. Otherwise, the madhhab is that it is permissible with a niyyah preceding the commencement with its prior condition, whether he is able to respond without thought or not. For this reason, it is said in al-Khaniyah and al-Khulasah: If one intends before commencing—from Muhammad that if he intended at the time of wudu to pray Zuhr or Asr with the imam and did not occupy himself after the niyyah with something not of the same type as prayer, but when he reached the place of prayer the niyyah did not occur to him, his prayer is valid with that niyyah. Similarly, it is narrated from Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf. In al-Bada'i': It is narrated from Abu Yusuf regarding one who left his house intending the obligatory prayer in congregation, and when he reached the imam he said takbir and the niyyah did not occur to him at that moment—that it is valid. Al-Karkhi said: I do not know anyone among our scholars who opposed Abu Yusuf in that. This indicates that the mere precedence of the original niyyah is sufficient, and the niyyah of specification for the obligatory prayers; simultaneity is not required, nor is keeping the intended prayer in mind during the prayer. Rather, the speech of Muhammad indicates that simultaneity of niyyah with takbir is not sufficient; rather, it is necessary to keep it in mind until the end of the prayer, because he said: If he needs to think after the query, his prayer is not valid. The scholars are unanimous that if one intends in his heart and does not speak, it is valid, as narrated by more than one. So what is in al-Khaniyah—'And according to al-Shafi'i, verbal mention is necessary'—is rejected.

Ruling on Verbalizing Niyyah: Hanafi Ikhtilaf and Reconciliation
Survey of Hanafi ikhtilaf on verbalizing niyyah with reconciliation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the various Hanafi positions on verbalizing niyyah and evaluate the author's reconciliation as 'bid'ah hasanah'.

Core Idea
Verbalizing niyyah is not from the Prophet; it is a later practice whose ruling ranges from mustahabb to bid'ah, reconciled as a 'good innovation' when done for focus.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq surveys the diverse opinions of Hanafi scholars on whether one should speak the intention (niyyah) aloud in prayer. It reveals a striking range: from mustahabb and sunnah to makruh and bid'ah. The author navigates these views, ultimately calling it a 'good bid'ah' when intended to gather resolve, while affirming that the heart intention is sufficient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the spectrum of rulings
The act is verbalizing the niyyah. The passage mentions multiple rulings: mustahabb, sunnah, bid'ah, makruh, permissible. Identify each view and its source.
The act itself is not part of the original prayer; it is an auxiliary practice.
2
Locate the sources of each opinion
The passage cites specific Hanafi texts: Munyat al-Musalli (mustahabb), al-Hidayah (good for resolve), al-Ikhtiyar (sunnah from Muhammad al-Shaybani), al-Qunyah (bid'ah unless needed), Sharh al-Munyah (makruh).
Fath al-Qadir is the strongest voice against it, calling it a bid'ah.
3
Analyse the strongest critique (Fath al-Qadir)
Fath al-Qadir states that no authentic or weak hadith from the Prophet or Companions supports verbalizing niyyah; only takbir is transmitted. This makes it a bid'ah.
This is the key dalil used by opponents.
4
Understand the author's reconciliation
The author calls it a 'bid'ah hasanah' (good innovation) when done with the intention to gather focus. He notes that even those who called it 'sunnah' likely meant a good practice, not a prophetic one.
The reconciliation preserves the principle that the heart intention is primary while acknowledging the benefit of verbalization.
5
Note the practical wording recommended
The passage gives recommended wording for different types of prayer (e.g., 'O Allah, I intend to pray... make it easy for me and accept it'). This shows that if one verbalizes, a specific du'a form is preferred over 'nawaytu'.
The wording is a du'a asking for ease, not a statement of intention per se.

وقد اختلف كلام المشايخ في التلفظ باللسان فذكر في منية المصلي أنه مستحب وهو المختار وصححه في المجتبى. وفي الهداية والكافي والتبيين أنه يحسن لاجتماع عزيمته، وفي الاختيار معزياً إلى محمد بن الحسن أن سنة، وهكذا في المحيط والبدائع. وفي القنية : إنه بدعة إلا أن لا يمكنه إقامتها في القلب إلا بإجرائها على اللسان فحينئذ يباح . ونقل عن بعضهم أن السنة الاقتصار على نية القلب فإن عبر عنه بلسانه جاز. ونقل في شرح المنية عن بعضهم الكراهة وطاهر ما في فتح القدير اختيار أنه بدعة فإنه قال قال بعض الحفاظ : لم يثبت عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من طريق صحيح ولا ضعيف أنه كان يقول عند الافتتاح أصلي كذا ولا عن أحد من كان عوناً على جمعه . ثم رأيته في التنجيس قال : والنية بالقلب لأنه عمله والتكلم لا معتبر به، ومن اختاره الحصكفي حيث قال : وهو أي عمل القلب أن يعلم عند الإرادة بداهة بلا تأمل أي صلاة يصلي حيث قيد بقوله «عند الإرادة دفعاً لما توهمه صاحب البحر . قوله : (وعند الشافعي رحمه الله لا بد من الذكر باللسان) فإنه ليس هذا مذهب الشافعي بل الذي ذكره الشافعية أنه سنة، وسيأتي عن شرح المنية أنه لم ينقل عن الأئمة الأربعة وفي شرح الشيخ اسمعيل سبق عن العيون وصرح به غير واحد أنه لا يشترط الذكر باللسان بالإجماع، فما في الخانية والنهاية ومجموع المسائل والمفتاح وغيرها. أنه من اختاره لتجتمع عزيمته ا هـ . وزاد في شرح المنية أنه لم ينقل عن الأئمة الأربعة أيضاً فتحرر من هذا أنه بدعة حسنة عند قصد جمع العزيمة، وقد استفاض ظهور العمل بذلك في كثير الأعصار في عامة الأمصار، ر، فلعل القائل بالسنية أراد بها الطريقة الحسنة لا طريقة النبي . وبقي الكلام في كيفية التلفظ بها، ففي المحيط ينبغي أن يقول اللهم أني أريد صلاة كذا فيسرها لي وتقبلها مني وهكذا في البدائع والحاوي. وفي القنية : إذا أراد النفل أو السنة يقول اللهم إني أريد الصلاة فيسرها لي وتقبلها مني وفي الفرض : اللهم أني أريد أن أصلي فرض الوقت أو فرض كذا فيسره لي وتقبله مني. وفي صلاة الجنازة اللهم أني أريد أن أصلي لك وأدعوا لهذا الميت فيسره لي وتقبله مني والمقتدي يقول اللهم أني أريد أن أصلي فرض الوقت متابعاً لهذا الإمام فيسره لي وتقبله مني ا هـ . وهذا كله يفيد أن التلفظ بها يكون بهذه العبارة لا بنحو «نويت» أو «أنوي كما عليه عامة المتلفظين بالنية من عامي وغيره، ولا يخفى أن سؤال التوفيق والقبول شيء آخر غير التلفظ بها على أنه قد ذكر غير واحد من مشايخنا في وجه ما ذكره محمد في كتاب الحج أن الحج لما كان مما يمتد ويقع فيه العوارض والموانع وهو عبادة عظيمة تحصل بأفعال شاقة استحب طلب التيسير والتسهيل من الله تعالى ولم يشرع مثل هذا الدعاء في الصلاة لأن أداءها في وقت يسير ا هـ. وهو صريح في نفي قياس الصلاة على الحج وفي المجتبى : من عجز من أحضار القلب في النية يكفيه اللسان ا هـ. وظاهره أن فعل اللسان يكون بدلاً عن فعل القلب، ومن المعلوم أن نصب الأبدال بالرأي لا يجوز في القنية : عزم على صلاة الظهر وجرى على لسانه نويت صلاة العصر يجزئه .
The words of the mashayikh have differed regarding verbalization with the tongue. It is mentioned in Munyat al-Musalli that it is mustahabb, and that is the chosen view, and it was declared sahih in al-Mujtaba. In al-Hidayah, al-Kafi, and al-Tabyin it is said that it is good for gathering one's resolve, and in al-Ikhtiyar attributed to Muhammad ibn al-Hasan that it is sunnah, and similarly in al-Muhit and al-Bada'i'. In al-Qunyah it is said that it is a bid'ah, unless one cannot establish it in the heart except by moving it on the tongue, then it becomes permissible. It is narrated from some that the sunnah is to restrict it to intention in the heart; if one expresses it with the tongue, it is permissible. In Sharh al-Munyah it is narrated from some that it is makruh. The apparent from Fath al-Qadir is the choice that it is a bid'ah, for he said: Some hadith scholars said: nothing authentic or weak is established from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) that he used to say at the opening 'I pray such-and-such,' nor from any of the Companions or Successors; rather, what is transmitted is that when he stood for prayer he said takbir, and this is a bid'ah. And it may be understood from the author's saying 'gathering of resolve' that it is not good for other than this purpose, because a person may be overcome by distraction, and if he mentions with his tongue it helps him gather it. Then I saw in al-Tanjees he said: Niyyah is with the heart because it is its action, and speech is not considered. And al-Haskafi chose this where he said: It is the action of the heart to know at the time of intention instinctively without reflection which prayer one is praying, as he restricted it with his statement 'at the time of intention' to refute what the author of al-Bahr assumed. His saying: 'And according to al-Shafi'i verbal mention is necessary' — this is not the madhhab of al-Shafi'i; rather, what the Shafi'is mention is that it is sunnah. It will come from Sharh al-Munyah that it is not transmitted from the four imams. In Sharh al-Shaykh Isma'il it is preceded from al-Uyun, and more than one explicitly stated that verbal mention is not required by consensus. So what is in al-Khaniyah, al-Nihayah, Majmu' al-Masa'il, al-Miftah, and others — that one chooses it to gather his resolve — [is incorrect]. In Sharh al-Munyah he added that it is also not transmitted from the four imams. So it is established from this that it is a good bid'ah when intending to gather one's resolve, and the practice of this has become widespread in many eras in most regions. Perhaps the one who said it is sunnah meant a good way, not the way of the Prophet. Then there remains discussion on how to verbalize it. In al-Muhit: he should say, 'O Allah, I intend to pray such-and-such, so make it easy for me and accept it from me.' Similarly in al-Bada'i' and al-Hawi. In al-Qunyah: if he intends nafl or sunnah, he says, 'O Allah, I intend to pray, so make it easy for me and accept it from me.' For obligatory: 'O Allah, I intend to pray the obligatory prayer of the time or such-and-such obligatory, so make it easy for me and accept it from me.' For janazah: 'O Allah, I intend to pray for You and supplicate for this deceased, so make it easy for me and accept it from me.' The follower says: 'O Allah, I intend to pray the obligatory prayer of the time following this imam, so make it easy for me and accept it from me.' All this indicates that the verbalization should be with this expression, not with 'nawaytu' or 'unawi' as common people do. And it is not hidden that asking for success and acceptance is something other than the verbalization itself. Moreover, more than one of our mashayikh mentioned in explanation of what Muhammad mentioned in the book of Hajj that since Hajj is something that extends and obstacles occur, and it is a great worship involving difficult actions, seeking facilitation and ease from Allah is recommended; such supplication was not prescribed for prayer because its performance is in a short time. This is explicit in negating analogizing prayer to Hajj. In al-Mujtaba: whoever is unable to bring his heart to the intention, his tongue suffices him. Its apparent meaning is that the action of the tongue becomes a substitute for the action of the heart. It is known that appointing substitutes by mere opinion is not permissible. In al-Qunyah: one resolved to pray Zuhr, but his tongue uttered 'I intend to pray Asr' — it suffices him.
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling of verbalizing the niyyah in prayer. The author presents a range of Hanafi opinions: some say it is mustahabb (chosen view), some say it is good for resolving distraction, some say it is sunnah (attributed to Muhammad al-Shaybani), some say it is a bid'ah unless needed, some say makruh. The strongest criticism comes from Fath al-Qadir, which calls it a bid'ah because there is no prophetic or companion precedent. The author then attempts to reconcile, calling it a 'good bid'ah' when done to gather focus. The passage also corrects a misattribution to al-Shafi'i, stating that the Shafi'i view is that it is sunnah, not obligatory. It then provides recommended wording for different types of prayers (nafl, fard, janazah, following imam) as found in Hanafi sources. Finally, it discusses the subtopic of whether the tongue can substitute for the heart when one is unable to have genuine intention; the author cautions that establishing substitutes by opinion is not allowed, but cites a case from al-Qunyah where a misuttered intention (Zuhr vs Asr) is overlooked.

Key Terms
بدعة حسنة (bid'ah hasanah): An innovation in practice that is considered good because it serves a legitimate purpose (gathering resolve) without contradicting a clear text.
عزيمة (azimah): Firm resolve; the mental focus one needs for prayer, which verbalization may help achieve.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Fath al-Qadir and some Hanafi authorities, what is the ruling on verbalizing the niyyah?
A) It is wajib.
B) It is sunnah mu'akkadah.
C) It is a bid'ah because there is no evidence from the Prophet or Companions.
D) It is makruh in all cases.

Key Takeaway
Verbalizing niyyah is not from the sunnah; it is a later practice that is permissible for focus but better avoided as a ritual innovation.

Sufficiency of Absolute Niyyah for Nafl, Sunnah, and Tarawih
Clarifying that a general intention suffices for supererogatory prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a general intention suffices for supererogatory prayers and apply the reasoning based on certainty and doubt.

Core Idea
For nafl, sunnah, and tarawih, a general intention is sufficient — specification is not required because the default is certainty.

In this lesson, we examine a concise ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: that absolute niyyah (e.g., 'I pray for Allah') suffices for all supererogatory prayers. The commentary in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the reasoning and confirms that this is the preferred view in the Hanafi school. Understanding this ruling clarifies a common point of confusion about intention in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayer categories
Note that the ruling covers three types: nafl (voluntary), sunnah (regular supererogatory), and tarawih (night prayers during Ramadan).
Sunnah here refers to ghayr mu'akkadah and mu'akkadah alike.
2
Understand the rationale for nafl
The term 'prayer' absolutely applies to nafl (the lesser type), so it is certain; any additional specification (e.g., number) is doubtful and not required.
This is agreed upon (muttafaq alayh) among Hanafis.
3
Extend to sunnah and tarawih
Sunnah and tarawih are essentially nafl that the Prophet consistently performed; the same ruling applies, though some earlier texts had differing views.
The preferred view (mufta bihi) is that absolute niyyah suffices.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Outside the Hanafi school, some require specification for sunnah mu'akkadah, but Hanafis treat all supererogatory prayers as nafl in this context.
The difference stems from how 'sunnah' is defined.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويكفيه مطلق النية للنفل والسنة والتراويح أما في النفل فمتفق عليه لأن مطلق اسم الصلاة ينصرف إلى النفل لأنه الأدنى فهو متيقن والزيادة مشكوك فيها، ولا فرق ينوي الصلاة أو الصلاة لله لأن المصلي لا يصلي لغير الله . وأما في السنة والتراويح فظاهر الرواية ما في الكتاب كما في الذخيرة والتنجيس وجعله في الهداية هو الصحيح. وفي المحيط : إنه قول عامة المشايخ وفي منية المفتي وخزانة الفتاوى إنه المختار، ورجحه في فتح القدير ونسبه إلى المحققين بأن معنى السنة كون النافلة مواظباً عليها من النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بعد الفريضة
His saying: (A general niyyah suffices him for nafl, sunnah, and tarawih. As for nafl, it is agreed upon because the absolute name of prayer applies to nafl, since it is the lower, so it is certain and the addition is doubtful. There is no difference between intending 'prayer' or 'prayer for Allah' because the one praying does not pray for other than Allah. As for sunnah and tarawih, the apparent of the riwayah is as in the book, as in al-Dhakhirah and al-Tanjees, and al-Hidayah declares it as the sahih. In al-Muhit it is the saying of the general mashayikh, and in Munyat al-Mufti and Khizanat al-Fatawa it is the chosen view, and it is preferred in Fath al-Qadir and attributed to the muhaqqiqun that the meaning of sunnah is that the nafl is a supererogatory act regularly performed by the Prophet (peace be upon him) after the obligatory prayer)
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage explains a ruling from the matn: for nafl (voluntary) prayers, sunnah (regular supererogatory) prayers, and tarawih, a general intention (e.g., 'I pray for Allah') suffices; one does not need to specify which specific nafl or sunnah. For nafl, this is agreed upon because the term 'prayer' absolutely refers to nafl (as the lesser type), and any additional specification is doubtful, so the default suffices. For sunnah and tarawih, the preferred position (mufta bihi) is that absolute niyyah is also sufficient, though there is some difference: the Zahir al-Riwayah as in the book (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) supports this, and it is chosen by many authorities including the author of Fath al-Qadir. The rationale: sunnah is essentially a nafl that the Prophet consistently performed, so it shares the ruling of nafl in this regard.

Key Terms
مطلق النية (mutlaq al-niyyah): An intention to pray without specifying the type or number of rak'ahs, e.g., 'I intend to pray for Allah.'
النفل (al-nafl): Voluntary prayer that is not obligatory; includes both non-stressed sunnah and additional nafl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For which type of prayer does the Hanafi madhhab absolutely require specification in the niyyah?
A) Nafl prayers
B) Sunnah prayers
C) Tarawih
D) Obligatory (fard) prayers

Key Takeaway
For supererogatory prayers (nafl, sunnah, tarawih), a general intention suffices; specification is not required because the default certainty of the category 'prayer' is enough.

The Ruling on Verbalizing Niyyah (Intention) in Prayer
Explains the proper wording of verbal niyyah and whether tongue can substitute for heart.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on verbal utterance of niyyah, explain its classification as a good innovation (bid'a hasana), and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Verbal utterance of niyyah is not required; it is a permissible good innovation to aid focus.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the common practice of saying the intention out loud before prayer. Many Muslims have adopted phrases like 'nawaytu an usalliya...' but is this necessary? The Hanafi school provides a clear answer: the heart's intention is sufficient, and any verbal expression is a later practice classified as a good innovation (bid'a hasana) when done to strengthen resolve. We will explore the evidence, the recommended wording, and the intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
The act in question is 'talfuz bi al-niyyah' (verbalizing the intention). Determine whether it is required (fard/wajib), recommended (sunnah), permissible (mubah), or prohibited (haram) according to the text.
The passage explicitly states it is not transmitted from the four imams and is a bid'a hasana.
2
Understand the Hanafi position and its evidence
The Hanafi school holds that intention is a condition (shart) of the heart, not a verbal act. The evidence is the hadith 'Actions are by intentions' (innama al-a'mal bi al-niyyat) and the lack of prophetic practice of verbalizing for prayer.
The text also rebuts the analogy to hajj, where supplication is recommended, because prayer is brief.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a difference within the Hanafi school: some scholars (like in al-Mujtaba) allow the tongue to substitute for the heart when one cannot concentrate, but others (including Ibn Nujaym) reject this as setting up substitutes by opinion.
The mufta bihi is that heart intention suffices; tongue substitution is not a general rule.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'i school requires verbal utterance along with heart intention. The Hamanafi response is that this lacks strong evidence and the prophetic practice did not include it.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both schools have valid methodologies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

From: 'He chose it so that his resolve may gather' etc. He added in Sharh al-Munya that it was not transmitted from the four imams either, so it is established that this is a good innovation (bid'a hasana) when intending to gather resolve, and the practice has become widespread in many ages in most regions. So perhaps the one who called it sunnah meant the good method, not the Prophet's method. Then the discussion remains about how to pronounce it. In al-Muhit: He should say: 'O Allah, I intend to perform such prayer, so make it easy for me and accept it from me.' Similarly in al-Bada'i' and al-Hawi. In al-Qunya: If he intends nafl or sunnah, he says: 'O Allah, I intend the prayer, so make it easy for me and accept it from me.' For fard: 'O Allah, I intend to pray the fard of the time or such fard, so make it easy for me and accept it from me.' For funeral prayer: 'O Allah, I intend to pray for You and supplicate for this deceased, so make it easy for me and accept it from me.' The follower says: 'O Allah, I intend to pray the fard of the time following this imam, so make it easy for me and accept it from me.' All this indicates that the utterance should be in these words, not like 'nawaytu' or 'anwi' as is common among the general public and others. It is not hidden that asking for success and acceptance is something other than the utterance itself. Some of our scholars mentioned regarding what Muhammad said in the Book of Hajj that since hajj is long and obstacles occur, and it is a great worship with difficult actions, asking Allah for ease is recommended, but such supplication was not legislated for prayer because its performance is in a short time. This clearly negates analogizing prayer to hajj. In al-Mujtaba: Whoever is unable to bring his heart to intention, his tongue suffices him. Its apparent meaning is that the action of the tongue serves as a substitute for the action of the heart. But it is known that setting up substitutes by opinion is not permissible. In al-Qunya: He resolved on Zuhr prayer but his tongue uttered 'I intend Asr prayer' – it suffices him.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the ruling on verbal utterance of niyyah (intention) for prayer. The commentator explains that the practice of speaking the intention loudly is not transmitted from the four Imams, but it is considered a good innovation (bid'a hasana) when done to strengthen resolve. The author then provides the recommended wording from various Hanafi works (al-Muhit, al-Bada'i', al-Hawi, al-Qunya) for different types of prayers: nafl/sunnah, fard, funeral, and for the follower. The key point is that one should use a supplication asking for ease and acceptance, not the common phrase 'nawaytu' or 'anwi'. The commentator distinguishes this supplication from the actual intention itself, noting that asking for tawfiq is different. He then addresses a potential analogy to hajj where supplication is recommended, but rejects it because prayer is short. Finally, he quotes al-Mujtaba saying that for those unable to concentrate in the heart, tongue suffices, but then objects that setting up substitutes by mere opinion is not valid, citing al-Qunya that if one intended Zuhr but uttered 'Asr', it suffices (implying the tongue's error doesn't invalidate the heart's intention). The overall teaching is that verbal wording is not a requirement; the heart's intention is primary, and the tongue's role is secondary and disputed.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): The intention in the heart to perform an act of worship; it is a condition for the validity of prayer.
بدعة حسنة (bid'a hasana): A good innovation; a practice not established by the Prophet ﷺ but permissible if it serves a good purpose and does not contradict the Shari'a.
تلفظ بالنية (talfuz bi al-niyyah): The act of pronouncing the intention verbally; according to this text, it is not required but can be done as a supplication for ease and acceptance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it was explicitly commanded by the Prophet.
B) Because it helps gather resolve and has become widespread, though not transmitted from the four imams.
C) Because it is a sunnah mu'akkadah.
D) Because it is a necessary substitute for heart intention.

Key Takeaway
The heart intention alone suffices for prayer; verbal utterance is a permissible aid, not a requirement.

General Intention Suffices for Nafl, Sunnah, and Tarawih
Explains that a general intention suffices for voluntary prayers including sunnah and tarawih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on intention for voluntary prayers and explain why a general intention suffices without specifying the type.

Core Idea
For nafl, sunnah, and tarawih, a general intention to pray is sufficient; specificity is not required.

When you stand for a voluntary prayer, do you need to specify whether it is sunnah, tarawih, or just nafl? The Hanafi school holds that a general intention to pray is enough. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this ruling and addresses why the Shafi'i requirement for specification is not accepted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of the ruling
The ruling concerns the intention (niyyah) for supererogatory prayers: nafl, sunnah, and tarawih. Determine what the passage says about the specificity of intention.
Intention is a condition (shart) for prayer, but its degree of specification is under discussion.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The Hanafi ruling is that a general intention (e.g., intending 'prayer' without specifying the type) suffices. The prayer is valid and counts as the intended voluntary act.
This is the mufta bihi position according to al-Hidayah and other major works.
3
Examine the proof
The proof is that the unqualified term 'prayer' applies first to nafl because nafl is the lowest (adna) and most basic form; any additional specification is doubtful and not required. For sunnah, the definition lies in the Prophet's regular practice, not in the intention.
The proof is linguistic (the absolute name applies to the simplest instance) and based on the nature of sunnah.
4
Note the inter-madhhab dispute
The Shafi'i school requires specification of the type of sunnah prayer in the intention. In contrast, the Hanafi school does not. The passage refutes the Shafi'i position.
The dispute is a legitimate ikhtilaf, but the Hanafi view is preferred.
5
Understand the practical consequence
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is that a Hanafi can pray two rak'ahs with a general intention and they will be counted as the sunnah of Fajr if performed at its time, even if he intended tahajjud. A Shafi'i would need to specify.
This eases the worshipper, as the description 'sunnah' is attained by the act itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بین أن قوله : (ويكفيه مطلق النية للنفل والسنة والتراويح أما في النفل فمتفق عليه لأن مطلق اسم الصلاة ينصرف إلى النفل لأنه الأدنى فهو متيقن والزيادة مشكوك فيها، ولا فرق ينوي الصلاة أو الصلاة لله لأن المصلي لا يصلي لغير الله . وأما في السنة والتراويح فظاهر الرواية ما في الكتاب كما في الذخيرة والتنجيس وجعله في الهداية هو الصحيح. وفي المحيط : إنه قول عامة المشايخ وفي منية المفتي وخزانة الفتاوى إنه المختار، ورجحه في فتح القدير ونسبه إلى المحققين بأن معنى السنة كون النافلة مواظباً عليها من النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بعد الفريضة اللسان عند الشافعي رحمه الله لا بد منه فيها غير صحيح .اهـ. قوله : (ومن المعلوم أن نصب الإبدال بالرأي لا يجوز أخذه من شرح المنية لابن أمير حاج وعبارته والعبد الضعيف له في هذا نظر لأن إقامة فعل في هذا مقام عمل القلب عند العجز عنه بدلاً من لا يكون لمجرد الرأي لأن الأبدال لا تنصب بالرأي وقد يسقط الشرط عند عدم القدرة عليه لا إلى بدل، وقد يسقط إلى بدل وقد يسقط المشروط بواسطة عدم القدرة على شرطه فإثبات أحد هذه الاحتمالات دون الباقي يحتاج إلى دليل، وأين الدليل هنا على إقامة فعل اللسان مقام فعل القلب في خصوص هذا الأمر من الشارع فليتأمل
It is clear that his saying: 'And general intention suffices for nafl, sunnah, and tarawih.' As for nafl, it is agreed upon because the absolute name of prayer applies to nafl since it is the lower; so it is certain and the increase is doubtful. There is no difference whether he intends 'prayer' or 'prayer for Allah' because the one who prays does not pray for other than Allah. As for sunnah and tarawih, the apparent position of the riwayah is what is in the book (Kanz), as in al-Dhakhira and al-Tanjis, and al-Hidayah considers it sahih. In al-Muhit: It is the saying of the general scholars, and in Munyat al-Mufti and Khizanat al-Fatawa it is the chosen view. It is preferred in Fath al-Qadir and attributed to the verifiers, because the meaning of sunnah is that the nafl is performed regularly by the Prophet ﷺ after the fard. As for the tongue being necessary in it according to al-Shafi'i, it is not correct. His saying: 'And it is known that setting up substitutes by opinion is not permissible' is taken from Sharh al-Munya by Ibn Amir Hajj, and his expression: 'The weak slave has a consideration in this because establishing an action in this place as a substitute for the heart's action when unable to do it as a substitute cannot be by mere opinion; for substitutes are not set up by opinion. And the condition may be dropped when there is inability to perform it without a substitute, or it may be dropped to a substitute, or the conditioned may be dropped due to inability to fulfill its condition. So establishing one of these possibilities over the rest requires evidence. And where is the evidence here for establishing the action of the tongue in place of the action of the heart in this particular matter from the Lawgiver? So let one reflect.'
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn statement 'And general intention suffices for nafl, sunnah, and tarawih.' The commentator Ibn Nujaym explains that for nafl (supererogatory prayer), it is agreed upon that simply intending 'prayer' suffices because the term 'prayer' unqualified most readily applies to nafl, which is the lesser form; any additional specificity is doubtful and thus not required. He also notes that intending 'prayer for Allah' is the same as intending 'prayer' since a Muslim prays only for Allah. For sunnah and tarawih prayers, the preferred view (mufta bihi) is that general intention suffices, as stated in al-Hidayah and other major works. The commentator then addresses a potential objection: some may say that verbal utterance is necessary for tarawih, but he refutes this by quoting al-Shafi'i's position as incorrect. He then delves into an intra-Hanafi debate about whether the tongue can substitute for the heart when the heart is unable to concentrate. The commentator expresses caution, arguing that such substitution cannot be established by mere opinion; it requires explicit evidence from the Shari'a, which is lacking. Thus, the relied-upon ruling is that general intention in the heart is sufficient, and verbalization is not a required substitute.

Key Terms
مطلق النية (mutlaq al-niyyah): An intention that is unspecified; for nafl and sunnah, intending merely 'prayer' is sufficient without specifying the exact type.
سنة (sunnah): Here meaning a regular supererogatory prayer (nafl) that the Prophet consistently performed; its description is attained by the action itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a general intention to pray is sufficient for all voluntary prayers, including sunnah and tarawih, without needing to specify the type.

Specification of Intention Required for Fard Prayers
Establishes that ta'yin (specification) is a condition for fard prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the requirement of ta'yin (specification) in the intention for fard prayers and explain its evidentiary basis from the hadith.

Core Idea
For a fard prayer, you must intend which specific prayer — 'Actions are by intentions' demands it.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the commentator Marghinani explains that for obligatory prayers, the intention must specify which prayer is being performed. Unlike supererogatory prayers where a general intention suffices, the differences among fard obligations require clear specification. The hadith of intentions serves as the primary evidence, and various ways of phrasing the intention are examined.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its nature
First, locate the statement that specification (ta'yin) is a condition (shart) for fard prayers. Note that this is presented as a ruling from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq.
2
Locate the evidence (dalil)
The commentator cites the hadith 'إنما الأعمال بالنيات'. Identify the source and note its transmission and textual category (mutawatir in meaning, but the wording is from ahad hadith).
Hadith is agreed upon by Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (indication of the ruling)
Explain how the hadith proves the need for specification: the phrase 'by intentions' means that the validity of an action depends on the intention corresponding to the specific act. Since fard prayers differ, one must intend the specific one.
The hadith is general in wording but specific in application due to the differences in obligations.
4
Analyze the scope of specification phrasing
The passage discusses two ways to specify: linking to the day (e.g., 'Asr today') or linking to the time (e.g., 'fard of the time'). Examine the conditions and disagreements, especially the restriction from Fath al-Qadir when time exits and one forgets.
Linking to the day is always valid; linking to the time is valid only if the time has not exited or if the person remembers.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
Based on the majority of Hanafi sources, specification is required. The most reliable method is to name the specific prayer (e.g., 'I intend Zuhr') or link clearly to the day. The phrase 'fard of the time' is acceptable only when the time is known and not exited.
The commentator favors the view from al-Zahiriyya that linking to the day suffices even after time exits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

His saying: 'And for fard, its specification is a condition, like Asr for example, because the fard prayers differ, so specification is necessary due to his ﷺ saying: 'Indeed, actions are by intentions.' He (the author of Kanz) gave it absolute scope, so it includes when one links it to the day, like 'Asr today', whether the time has exited or not, because at most it is a make-up (qada) with the intention of performance (ada'), and that is permissible according to the sahih. This is indicated by the case of the prisoner: if he is uncertain about Ramadan and estimates a month and fasts, and it turns out to be after Ramadan, this is a make-up with the intention of performance. Thus in al-Zahiriyya. And it includes when one links it to the time, like 'Asr of the time' or 'fard of the time'. The commentator made this restriction only for 'fard of the time', reasoning that 'fard of the time' is...
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the requirement of ta'yin (specification) in the intention for fard (obligatory) prayers. The base text (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) states that specification is a condition. The commentator provides the evidence from the hadith 'Actions are by intentions' (innama al-a'malu bi al-niyyat), which implies that one must intend the specific act. The author then discusses how to specify: one can link the intention to the day (e.g., 'Asr today') or to the time (e.g., 'Asr of this time'). The ruling is absolute: even if the time has exited and one intends with such phrasing, it counts as qada (make-up) and is valid. The commentator supports this with the Hanafi example of a prisoner (asir) who fasts an estimated month for Ramadan and it turns out to be after Ramadan; his fast is valid as qada with an intention of ada'. However, a nuance from Fath al-Qadir is noted: if one says 'fard of the time' and the time has exited while he forgot, it does not suffice. This restriction is applied only to the phrase 'fard of the time', not to linking to the day. The passage emphasizes the importance of clear intention for obligatory prayers, contrasting with the earlier leniency for supererogatory prayers.

Key Terms
تعيين النية (ta'yin al-niyyah): Specifying the exact obligatory prayer in the intention (e.g., Zuhr, Asr) as a condition for validity.
فرض الوقت (fard al-waqt): An intention phrased as 'the fard of the time' which may suffice if the time is known, but is problematic if the time has exited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Intention after the time is invalid.

Key Takeaway
For obligatory prayers, the intention must specify which prayer is being performed; a general intention does not fulfill the obligation.

Intention for Obligatory and Sunnah Prayers: Specification and Description
Condition of specifying fard and sunnah by act

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the condition of specifying obligatory prayers and how the description of sunnah can be acquired by the act itself without a separate intention.

Core Idea
Specifying the obligatory prayer is required; sunnah description is obtained by performing the act properly, even without intending 'sunnah'.

The intention (niyyah) is central to prayer, but the Hanafi school distinguishes between obligatory and supererogatory prayers regarding what must be specified. This passage clarifies that for fard prayers, one must specify which prayer (e.g., 'Asr), while for sunnah prayers, the act itself can confer the description of sunnah. It then applies this principle to tarawih, Fajr, and Jumu'ah, addressing practical questions that arise in daily worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for obligatory prayers
Note that the author states ta'yin (specifying which obligatory prayer) is a condition for its validity. For example, one must intend 'Asr specifically, not just any prayer.
This applies to all fard prayers, including the five daily prayers and Jumu'ah.
2
Understand how sunnah description is acquired
If a worshipper performs an act that is commonly recognized as a sunnah prayer (e.g., two rak'ahs before Fajr), the description of sunnah applies even if he did not intend 'sunnah' explicitly. The attribute is based on the manner of the act, not the intention.
This is a distinctive Hanafi position; other schools require specifying 'sunnah' in the intention.
3
Analyze the tarawih intention dispute
The passage quotes Qadikhan and Munyat al-Musalli: some scholars say each pair (shaf') of tarawih needs a separate intention, but the most correct view is that one intention covers all pairs, as the entire tarawih is considered one prayer.
The precautionary view is to intend tarawih or sunnah of the time.
4
Apply the principle to Fajr and Jumu'ah sunnah
If one prays tahajjud after dawn, it counts as sunnah of Fajr because voluntary prayer is disliked then. Similarly, four rak'ahs prayed after Jumu'ah as a precaution (in case Jumu'ah is invalid) count as sunnah of Jumu'ah if Jumu'ah is confirmed, according to the majority.
These applications show the Hanafi flexibility in intention when the act is performed in the proper time and manner.

والتراويح وللفرض شرط تعيينه كالعصر مثلاً والمقتدي ينوي المتابعة أيضاً وللجنازة المعينة أو قبلها، فإذا أوقع المصلي النافلة في ذلك المحل صدق عليه أنه فعل الفعل المسمى سنة. فالحاصل أن وصف السنة يحصل بنفس الفعل الذي فعله له وهو إنما كان يفعل على ما سمعت فإنه لم يكن ينوي السنة بل الصلاة لله تعالى فعل أن وصف السنة ثبت بعد فعله على ذلك الوجه تسمية منا بفعله المخصوص لا أنه وصف يتوقف حصوله على نيته. وذكر قاضيخان في فتاواه في فصل التراويح اختلاف المشايخ في السنن والتراويح، والصحيح أنها لا تتأدى بنية الصلاة وبنية التطوع لأنها صلاة مخصوصة فتجب مراعاة الصفة للخروج عن العهدة، وذلك بأن ينوي السنة أو متابعة النبي ، وهل يحتاج لكل شفع من التراويح أن ينوي ويعين؟ قال بعضهم يحتاج لأن كل شفع صلاة، والأصح أنه لا يحتاج لأن الكل بمنزلة صلاة واحدة ا هـ . فقد اختلف التصحيح فلذا قال في منية المصلي: والاحتياط في التراويح أن ينوي التراويح أو سنة الوقت أو قيام الليل وفي السنة ينوي السنة ا هـ . أطلق المصنف في السنة فشمل سنة الفجر حتى لو صلى ركعتين تهجداً ثم تبين أنه صلاهما بعد طلوع الفجر عن السنة. وفي آخر العمدة للصدر الشهيد : إذا صلى أربع ركعات تطوعاً قبل الفجر فوقع ركعتان بعد الطلوع يحتسب من ركعتي الفجر ا.هـ. وفي الخلاصة : وبه يفتى وفيه نظر لأن السنة إنما تكون بتحريمة مبتدأة بعد الطلوع ولم تحصل وقد قالوا في سجود السهو : إنه لو قام إلى الخامسة بعد القعود على رأس الرابعة ساهياً فإنه يضم السادسة ولا ينوبان عن الظهر لما قلنا فكذا في سنة الفجر اللهم إلا أن يقال : لما كان التنفل مكروهاً في الفجر جعلناهما سنة بخلافه في الظهر. ولا يخفى أن الأربع التي تصلى بعد الجمعة على أنها آخر ظهر عليه للشك في الجمعة إذا تبين صحة الجمعة فإنها تنوب عن سنتها على قول الجمهور لأنه يلغو الوصف ويبقى الأصل، وبه تتأدى السنة وعلى قول البعض لا تنوب لاشتراط التعيين.
And the tarawih (prayers). For the obligatory prayer, specifying it is a condition, like Asr for example. The follower also intends following (the imam). For the funeral prayer, (he intends) the specific deceased or before it. So if the worshiper performs the supererogatory prayer in that place, it is true of him that he performed the act called sunnah. The conclusion is that the description of sunnah is acquired by the act itself which he performed for it, and he was only doing as you have heard, for he did not intend the sunnah but rather prayer for Allah the Exalted. So the description of sunnah is established after his act in that manner, a designation from us for his specific act; it is not a description whose attainment depends on his intention. Qadikhan mentioned in his Fatāwā in the section on tarawih: The mashāyikh differed concerning the sunan and tarawih. The correct view is that they are not fulfilled by the intention of prayer and the intention of supererogation because they are specific prayers, so observing the description is necessary for discharge of obligation, and that is by intending the sunnah or following the Prophet. And is it necessary for each pair (shafʿ) of tarawih to intend and specify? Some said it is necessary because each pair is a prayer. The most correct is that it is not necessary because all are like one prayer. End quote. So the verification differed, hence the author of Munyat al-Muṣallī said: The precaution in tarawih is to intend tarawih or the sunnah of the time or night prayer, and for the sunnah to intend the sunnah. End quote. The author (of Kanz) gave absolute expression for sunnah, so it includes the sunnah of Fajr, even if one prayed two rakʿahs as tahajjud then it becomes clear that he prayed them after dawn (they count) as sunnah. And in the end of al-ʿUmdah by al-Ṣadr al-Shahīd: If one prayed four rakʿahs voluntarily before Fajr, and two rakʿahs occurred after dawn, they count as the two rakʿahs of Fajr. End quote. In al-Khulāṣah: And this is the fatwa, but there is a consideration because the sunnah is only by a new taḥrīmah after dawn, which did not occur. And they said in forgetting sajdah: If one stood for the fifth after sitting at the end of the fourth forgetfully, he adds the sixth, and they do not substitute for the ẓuhr for what we said; similarly for sunnah of Fajr, unless it is said: Since voluntary prayer is disliked at Fajr, we make them sunnah, unlike ẓuhr. And it is not hidden that the four prayed after Jumuʿah as a replacement for ẓuhr due to doubt about Jumuʿah, if Jumuʿah is confirmed valid, they substitute for its sunnah according to the majority because the description is nullified and the original remains, and thereby the sunnah is fulfilled; according to some they do not substitute because specification is required.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the conditions of prayer, specifically regarding intention (niyyah). The author first states that for obligatory prayers, specifying which prayer is intended is a condition, giving the example of ʿAṣr. For the follower (muqtadī), he must also intend to follow the imam. For the funeral prayer (janāzah), one must intend the specific deceased or at least intend before starting. The author then turns to supererogatory prayers (nāfilah) and explains that if someone performs a prayer that is commonly known as a sunnah prayer, the description of 'sunnah' applies to his act even if he did not specifically intend 'sunnah' but merely intended prayer. This is because the attribute of being a sunnah is acquired by the specific manner of the act, not by the intention. The passage then discusses the tarāwīḥ prayer, quoting Qāḍīkhān's Fatāwā: the correct view is that tarāwīḥ is not fulfilled by a general intention of prayer or supererogation; one must intend specifically tarāwīḥ or following the Prophet. There is a disagreement whether each pair (shafʿ) requires a separate intention; the most correct view is that it does not, as all pairs are like one prayer. The author of Munyat al-Muṣallī advises precaution: one should intend tarāwīḥ, or the sunnah of the time, or night prayer. For regular sunnah prayers, one should intend the specific sunnah. The author then applies this to the sunnah of Fajr: if one prays two rakʿahs of tahajjud before Fajr, and then realizes that they were actually after dawn, they count as the sunnah of Fajr. This is supported by a quote from al-ʿUmdah by al-Ṣadr al-Shahīd, though al-Khulāṣah raises an objection because the sunnah requires a new intention after dawn. The passage resolves this by noting that since voluntary prayer is disliked after dawn, the two rakʿahs are deemed sunnah, unlike the case of ẓuhr. Finally, a parallel case: four rakʿahs prayed after Jumuʿah as a precaution (in case Jumuʿah is invalid) count as the sunnah of Jumuʿah if Jumuʿah is confirmed, according to the majority, because the original intention (replacement for ẓuhr) is overridden.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention in the heart to perform a specific act of worship.
تعيين (ta'yīn): Specifying which particular prayer is intended (e.g., Fajr, Zuhr).
سنة (sunnah): A supererogatory prayer that the Prophet regularly performed, here acquired by the act itself.
تراويح (tarāwīḥ): The night prayers of Ramadan, consisting of multiple pairs of rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if someone prays two rak'ahs of tahajjud before Fajr and later realizes they were after dawn, do they count as the sunnah of Fajr?
A) No, because sunnah requires a new intention after dawn
B) Yes, because voluntary prayer is disliked at that time, so they become sunnah
C) No, because tahajjud and sunnah are different
D) Yes, but only if he intended sunnah from the beginning

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, specifying the prayer is a condition for obligatory prayers, but for sunnah prayers, the description can be acquired by the act itself, even without explicit 'sunnah' intention, especially when the alternative would be disliked.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
12 min
Intention of 'Zuhr al-Waqt' When Unsure of Time Exit: Hanafi Intra-School Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on intention wording and time awareness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two Hanafi positions on the validity of intending 'zuhr al-waqt' when unaware vs. doubtful of the time exit, and apply the dispute to a real scenario.

Core Idea
Intending 'zuhr al-waqt' fails when unaware of time exit, but is valid in doubt according to the chosen view.

In this passage, the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq navigates a nuanced internal Hanafi dispute about the validity of prayer when the worshipper intends 'zuhr al-waqt' (the zuhr of the time) but the time has actually passed. The central question is whether ignorance (adam al-'ilm) and doubt (shakk) are treated the same or differently. The passage reveals two opposing positions among later Hanafi authorities, and the author attempts to reconcile them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes between two situations: (a) the person is unaware that the time has exited, and (b) the person is doubtful about the exit.
Unawareness means the person firmly believes the time remains; doubt means uncertainty.
2
State the positions on each scenario
Some authorities (al-Fath, Ibn Malik) rule that intending 'zuhr al-waqt' is invalid in both scenarios. Others ('Umdat al-Mufti, al-Ashbah) rule that it is invalid in unawareness but valid in doubt.
The second group is supported by the chosen view according to al-Muhit.
3
Examine the evidence for each position
The first group argues that the definite article 'al' refers to the actual time, which has changed. The second group relies on the principle that qada' can be performed with the intention of ada' in doubt, and that 'al' refers to the time in the person's mind.
The linguistic analysis of 'al' is crucial.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If one is unaware and prays zuhr with 'zuhr al-waqt', the prayer must be repeated. If doubtful, some scholars say it is valid, avoiding repetition.
This has direct impact on whether the person must repeat a prayer.
5
Evaluate the author's resolution
The author of al-Bahr attempts to reconcile by distinguishing between ignorance and doubt, but ultimately concedes that the two positions are irreconcilable, and the chosen view is permissibility in doubt.
The author sides with the distinction but acknowledges the conflict.

خروج الوقت غير الظهر علة لعدم جواز نية ظهر الوقت وفرض الوقت بلا تقدير فلا حاجة إلى الشك ومع
Book of Prayer - Chapter on Conditions of Prayer. This case is other than Zuhr, so the intention of ‘Asr of the time should be valid even if the time has exited, and the time is like the day, as is not hidden. And an exception from the fard of the time is Friday, for it is a substitute for the fard of the time, not itself, so Friday is not valid with the intention of the fard of the time unless he believes it is the fard of the time. And it includes what... or fard of the time and the time remains for the existence of specification, so if the time had exited and he is unaware of it, it is not valid because the fard of the time in this case is other than Zuhr. End. That is, and likewise Zuhr of the time, for he made it a restriction in both, as you see, and the difference between Zuhr of the time and Zuhr of the day is needless of explanation. End of the statement of al-Nahr. Some virtuous ones said: And whoever reflects finds the truth with the author of al-Bahr, because if the time of ‘Asr enters and he is unaware of it, then in the time of ‘Asr there is a prayer called the fard of the time, so it is not valid with the intention of the fard of the time due to confusion, and there is no prayer called Zuhr of the time, so the situation is not confused, so it must be valid. And al-Zayla‘i’s wording is open to what he understood in al-Bahr, rather it is close for one who ponders. End. But Shaykh Isma‘il, the author of al-Bahr, objected before seeing the statement of al-Nahr that the apparent meaning of the wording is that the restriction is for both, as was done in al-Fath. And as for his taking that from the statement of al-Tabyin in the reasoning because the fard of the time is not sound, because the statement of al-Tabyin after it, 'And if he intended the Zuhr of his day, it is valid absolutely' gives the opposite. End. Then he quoted from al-Nihayah, al-Kifayah, al-Khulasah, and others similar to al-Zayla‘i’s wording, then said: And the summary is that these wordings are not devoid of indication that Zuhr of the time is like the fard of the time, not like the Zuhr of his day, in accordance with what al-Fath mentioned and al-Tabyin understood. He said: Then I saw Ibn Malik, who is older than the author of al-Fath, explicitly stated that as well, saying: In al-Muhit al-Awwal concerning the intention of fard, for example, that he says 'I intend Zuhr of the day' because if he said 'Zuhr of the time' or 'its fard' and the time was outside while he is unaware, it does not suffice him. But if he said 'Zuhr of the day', it suffices him, whether the time is outside or remaining. End. But in ‘Umdat al-Mufti: And if he doubts the exit of the time and intends the fard of the time, it is not valid because it may be Zuhr or ‘Asr. And if he intends Zuhr of the time or ‘Asr of the time, it is valid based on the position that making up with the intention of performance and performance with the intention of making up is valid according to the chosen view, mentioned in al-Muhit. End. But this contradicts the exclusivity of al-Tabyin that relief from doubt is in Zuhr of the day, unless it is interpreted in the way adopted by the author of al-Bahr of disconnecting Zuhr of the time from the reasoning. But the verification is that there is a difference between the case of doubt and the case of our issue in terms of the presence of doubt in it that does not purify the intention, unlike the cases of forgetfulness and lack of knowledge. So we conclude that the intention of Zuhr of the time and fard of the time are not sufficient in the case of lack of knowledge of the time’s exit, as in the commentary of Ibn Malik and al-Fath, and the wordings of the mentioned books imply it, and the author of al-Fath mentioned forgetfulness instead of lack of knowledge. And the first [i.e., Zuhr of the time] suffices in the case of doubt of its exit, as stated in al-‘Umdah. As for Zuhr of the day, it suffices in the case of lack of knowledge, as they explicitly stated, and it is also stated in al-Walwaljiyyah, and in the case of doubt as stated by al-‘Attabi and al-Tabyin. And evidence for the difference we mentioned between the two cases of doubt and lack of knowledge is the statement of Khazanat al-Fatawa: And in al-‘Attabi: He should intend Zuhr of his day, and likewise every time he doubts its exit. And they differed on whether the timeliness is affected by the intention of making up; the chosen view is that it is valid if in his heart is the fard of the time. If the time exits while he is unaware and he intends Zuhr of his day, it is valid. End. For without the difference, it would be repetition. And the statement of al-Mujtaba: And if he intends the fard of the time after it has exited, it is not valid; and if he doubts its exit and intends the fard of the time, it is valid. The contradiction: if he intends ‘Asr without a restriction, there is a difference concerning it. In al-Zahiriyyah: If he intends Zuhr, it is not valid because this time accepts both Zuhr of this day and another Zuhr. And some say: It is valid, and that is correct because the time is specific for it. This applies if he is performing on time. If he is making up, then if he prays after the time exits while unaware of the exit, based on the permissibility of making up with the intention of performance. End. Then I found the author of al-Nahr said etc. End. The statement of Shaykh Isma‘il, may Allah have mercy on him. I say: And it is mentioned in al-Ashbah wa al-Naza’ir from al-Tatar Khaniyyah: Every time one doubts its exit and intends, for example, Zuhr of the time, then it turns out to have exited, the chosen view is permissibility. End. And likewise in the text of al-Munyah from al-Muhit, and the explicit statement that it is the chosen view, but with the addition of the building mentioned from ‘Umdat al-Mufti. And al-Halabi did not see the difference between doubt and lack of knowledge, so he objected to al-Munyah with what is in Fath al-Qadir and al-Khulasah, then said: From this it is known that what is chosen in al-Muhit is not the chosen view. End. And Ibn Amir Hajj was very odd where he ruled that what is in al-Munyah is a mistake, not supported by the apparent meaning nor what is recorded in the books of the madhhab, as al-Hamawi narrated in his gloss on al-Ashbah. From him, when he knew of the transmission of the mentioned branch in al-Tatar Khaniyyah, ‘Umdat al-Mufti, and al-Muhit, for the author of al-Munyah is trustworthy, not to be faulted without verification, and its existence in these reliable books contradicts that. And know that the summary of what Shaykh Isma‘il mentioned is repelling the objection to al-Zayla‘i’s exclusive statement and reconciling his statement if interpreted as he established in al-Nahr and the statement of al-‘Umdah, but each has a point. As for the first, if interpreted according to what al-Bahr said, then there is nothing in al-Zayla‘i’s statement indicating that the intention of Zuhr of the time is like the intention of Zuhr of the day. Rather, the specification of the relief to the second indicates that the first is not so, so the objection remains. And because what he mentioned of the difference between doubt and lack of knowledge does not help in repelling the contradiction. And what appears to me is that they are two opposing statements, as indicated by the statements of the commentators of al-Munyah. And al-Zayla‘i’s statement at the end: 'And if he intends Zuhr of his day, it is valid absolutely, and it is a relief for one who doubts the exit of the time' End. While the beginning of his statement is about lack of knowledge, so this indicates that he did not see a difference between it and doubt. And the contradiction between al-Zayla‘i’s statement and al-Fath and those who agree with them and between the statement of al-‘Umdah, al-Ashbah, and al-Munyah is not removed by the difference he mentioned. Rather, it confirms the contradiction and rules that they are two divergent statements, as we said. And its clarification: If he is unaware of the time’s exit and intends Zuhr of the time, then in his assumption the time remains, so his intention refers to the time of Zuhr; this intention is not permissible. So if he is doubtful of its exit, he is more deserving of non-permissibility. Thus, the ruling of permissibility in this contradicts the ruling of non-permissibility in the first. So where is the reconciliation? And what he used as evidence from the statement of al-Khazanah and al-Mujtaba does not indicate a repelling of the contradiction, though it does indicate an original difference. And arguing for the difference between them is unnecessary because no one denies it. And the statement of al-Khazanah is not about our issue because its summary is that there is no difference in the intention of Zuhr of the time between the two cases of doubt and lack of knowledge. And as for lack of knowledge, the statement of al-Mujtaba does not address it. So it is established that they are two statements, and that the chosen view is contrary to what is in al-Munyah and al-‘Umdah, as al-Halabi said. Then the verification is that al-Zayla‘i’s reasoning applies to both cases because the 'al' in 'al-waqt' – as al-Halabi said – is for the specific known time, not for the genus. So if he does not know that the time has exited and intends Zuhr of the time, it is not valid because with the exit of the time, Zuhr is not specific, for it is not that present specific fard of the time but rather the fard of another time. So al-Zayla‘i’s statement 'because the fard of the time in this case' i.e., the case of time exit, is other than Zuhr, is the reason for the non-permissibility of intending Zuhr of the time and fard of the time without estimation, so there is no need for doubt and...
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage is a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute about the validity of intention when one intends 'zuhr al-waqt' (the zuhr of the time) or 'fard al-waqt' (the obligatory prayer of the time) while being unaware that the time has actually exited, or when doubtful about the exit. The core issue is whether such an intention is valid if the time has passed without the person's knowledge. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and others argue that when one is unaware of the time exit, intending 'zuhr al-waqt' is invalid because the actual fard of that time is no longer zuhr (it is asr). However, if one intends 'zuhr al-yawm' (the zuhr of that day), it is valid regardless of whether the time has exited or not, because the intention is linked to the day, not the specific time. The dispute arises when comparing the case of ignorance (adam al-'ilm) with the case of doubt (shakk). Some sources, like 'Umdat al-Mufti and al-Ashbah, permit intending 'zuhr al-waqt' in doubt, while others like al-Fath and Ibn Malik prohibit it in ignorance. The text attempts to reconcile these positions but ultimately concludes that there are two divergent opinions. The analysis delves into the linguistic nuance of the definite article 'al' in 'al-waqt', clarifying that it refers to the specific time (al-'ahd) not the genus, which explains why intending 'zuhr al-waqt' fails when the time has changed. The passage is a critical refinement (hāshiya) that challenges earlier commentaries and seeks to resolve the apparent contradiction between different Hanafi authorities. The author sides with the view that when unaware, 'zuhr al-waqt' is invalid, but when doubtful, it is valid based on the chosen position that allows qada' with the intention of ada'.

Key Terms
ظهر الوقت (zuhr al-waqt): Intention of 'the zuhr of the time', referring to the prayer that is due at that specific time period.
ظهر اليوم (zuhr al-yawm): Intention of 'the zuhr of this day', which is clear and remains valid even if the time has exited because it is linked to the day, not the specific time.
فرض الوقت (fard al-waqt): Intention of 'the obligatory prayer of the time', which is ambiguous if the time has changed.
شك (shakk): Doubt; uncertainty about whether the time has exited or not.
عدم العلم (adam al-'ilm): Lack of knowledge; being unaware that the time has actually exited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of authorities cited in the passage, what is the ruling when a person intends 'zuhr al-waqt' and is unaware that the time has exited?
A) The prayer is valid.
B) The prayer is invalid because the fard of the time is no longer zuhr.
C) The prayer is valid only if he also intended 'zuhr al-yawm'.
D) The prayer is invalid only if he was certain.

Key Takeaway
The intention 'zuhr al-waqt' is insufficient when the time has exited without the person's knowledge; but in doubt, the preferred view permits it, reflecting the nuanced application of usul principles in Hanafi fiqh.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
10 min
Intending the Time-Specific Prayer When Time is Uncertain
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of intending 'Zuhr of the time' when time is uncertain

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on intending a time-specific prayer when the time is uncertain and evaluate the role of heart-knowledge in resolving the dispute.

Core Idea
When the time is uncertain, the validity of intending 'al-waqt' depends on knowing which prayer is due in the heart.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq delves into a nuanced disagreement within the Hanafi school: can a person validly intend 'Zuhr of the time' if the time for Zuhr has actually passed? The discussion pivots on the interpretation of the definite article in 'al-waqt' and the distinction between doubt (shakk) and ignorance (jahl). Ibn Nujaym navigates multiple opinions, ultimately settling on a pragmatic criterion: what matters is the intention in the heart, not the external reality of the time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The dispute centers on the validity of intending 'Zuhr of the time' (niyyat zuhr al-waqt) when the time for Zuhr has actually exited or is doubtful. Is the intention sound or not?
2
Follow the two main positions
One position (al-Halabi, al-Khulasa) says it is invalid because the definite article 'al' indicates a specific time (al-‘ahd) and that time has passed. Another position (al-Muhit, al-Tatarkhaniyyah) says it is permissible, especially in case of doubt. Note the distinction between doubt (shakk) and lack of knowledge (adam al-‘ilm).
3
Examine the arguments and rationale
Al-Halabi argues that no difference exists between doubt and ignorance; both invalidate the intention because the time is no longer specific. The opposing view cites Shams al-A'imma who says one should intend 'the prayer due on him' – if it is a current prayer, it is valid; if a make-up, also valid. The author supports this by stating that the condition of knowing in one's heart which prayer one is praying cuts off the dispute.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and its practical effect
The author concludes that the chosen position is permissibility based on heart-knowledge. This means that even if the person is mistaken about the time, as long as his heart is set on the prayer that is actually due on him, the intention is valid. This provides a practical resolution for worshippers in uncertainty.

إذا نوى العصر بلا قيد وفيه خلاف ; ففي الظهيرية : لو نوى الظهر لا يجوز لأن هذا الوقت كما يقبل ظهر هذا اليوم يقبل ظهر آخر . وقيل : يجوز وهو الصحيح لأن الوقت متعين له. هذا إذا كان مؤدياً، فإن كان قاضياً، فإن صلى بعد خروج الوقت وهو لا يعلم بخروج بناء على جواز القضاء بنية الأداء .اهـ. ثم وجدت صاحب النهر قال الخ .اهـ. كلام الشيخ اسمعيل رحمه الله . أقول : وذكر في الأشباه والنظائر عن التتارخانية : كل وقت شك في خروجه فنوى ظهر الوقت مثلاً فإذا هو قد خرج المختار الجواز اهـ. وكذا في متن المنية عن المحيط. والتصريح بأنه المختار لكن بزيادة البناء المار عن عمدة المفتي وكان الحلبي لم ير الفرق بين الشك وعدم العلم فاعترض المنية بما في فتح القدير والخلاصة ثم قال : فعلم من هذا أن ما اختاره في المحيط غير المختار اهـ. وأغرب ابن أمير حاج حيث حكم بأن ما في المنية غلط لا يساعده الوجه ولا المسطور في كتب المذهب كما نقله الحموي في حاشية الأشباه . عنه لما علمت من نقله الفرع المذكور في التتارخانية وعمدة المفتي والمحيط، فإن صاحب المنية ثقة لا يعز وبغير تثبت ووجوده في هذه الكتب المعتبرة ينافي ذلك واعلم أن حاصل ما ذكره الشيخ اسمعيل دفع الإيراد على حصر الزيلعي ودفع بين كلامه لو حمل على ما قرره في النهر وكلام العمدة وفي كل نظر; أما الأول فلأنه لو حمل على ما قاله في البحر لا يكون في كلام الزيلعي ما يدل على أن نية ظهر الوقت كنية ظهر اليوم، بل تخصيص المخلص بالثاني يدل على أن الأول ليس كذلك، فالإيراد باق ولأن ما ذكره من التغاير بين وعدم العلم لا يجدي في دفع المنافاة، والذي يظهر لي أنهما قولان متقابلان كما دل عليه كلام شارحي المنية. وقول الزيلعي آخراً ولو نوى ظهر يومه يجوز مطلقاً وهو مخلص لمن يشك في خروج الوقت اهـ. مع أن صدر كلامه في عدم العلم فهذا يدل على أنه لم ير الفرق بينه وبين الشك ولا يظهر دفع المنافاة بين كلام الزيلعي والفتح ومن وافقهما وبين كلام العمدة والأشباه والمنية بما ذكره من الفرق، بل هو يؤكد المنافاة ويحكم بأنهما قولان متباينان كما قلنا وبيانه أنه إذا كان غير عالم بخروج الوقت ونوى ظهر الوقت فالذي في ظنه أن الوقت باقٍ فيكون مراده بالوقت وقت الظهر، هذا لا تجوز نيته فإذا كان شاكاً في خروجه يكون أولى في عدم الجواز. فالقول بالجواز في هذا ينافي القول بعدمه في الأول، فأين التوفيق؟ وما استدل به من عبارة الخزانة والمجتبى لا يدل على دفع المنافاة وإن دل على أصل التغاير على أن الاستدلال على التغاير بينهما مما لا حاجة إليه لأنه لا ينكره أحد. وعبارة الخزانة ليست مما نحن فيه لأن حاصلها أنه لا فرق في نية ظهر الوقت بين مسألتي الشك وعدم العلم على أن ليس في عبارة المجتبى التعرض لعدم العلم فثبت أنهما قولان، وأن المختار خلاف ما في النية والعمدة كما قاله الحلبي . ثم التحقيق أن تعليل الزيلعي يصلح لكل من المسألتين وذلك أن «أل» في الوقت - كما قال الحلبي - للعهد لا للجنس، فإذا لم يعلم بخروج الوقت، ونوى ظهر الوقت لا يجوز لأنه بخروج الوقت لا يتعين الظهر إذ ليس ذلك فرض الوقت الحاضر المعهود بل فرض الوقت غيره، فقول الزيلعي لأن محمداً فرض الوقت في هذه الحالة أي حالة خروج الوقت غير الظهر علة لعدم جواز نية ظهر الوقت وفرض الوقت بلا تقدير فلا حاجة إلى الوقت فنوى الظهر لا يجوز أيضاً. وذكر شمس الأئمة: ينوي صلاة عليه، فإن كانت وقتية فهي عليه، وإن كانت قضاء فهي عليه أيضاً ا.هـ. وهكذا صححه في فتح القدير معزياً إلى فتاوى العتابي لكن جزم في الخلاصة بعدم الجواز، وصححه السراج الهندي في شرح المغني فاختلف التصحيح كما ترى. وينبغي في مسألة شمس الأئمة أن لا يكون عليه صلاة غيرها وإلا فلا تعيين وأفاد أنه لو نوى شيئين فإنه لا يصح، فلو نوى فائتة ووقتية كما إذا فاتته الظهر فنوى في وقت العصر الظهر والعصر فإنه لا يصير شارعاً في واحدة منهما. وفي منية ما قاله في النهر، وقد ظهر من هذا التقرير أيضاً دفع ما قدمناه عن بعض الفضلاء كما لا يخفى . قوله : (وهكذا صححه الخ) راجع إلى قوله ،به وقيل يجوز وهو الصحيح وكذا استظهره في العناية ثم قال : وأقول : الشرط المتقدم وهو أن يعلم بقلبه أي صلاة يصلي يحسم مادة هذه المقالات وغيرها فإن العمدة عليه الحصول التمييز به وهو المقصود .اهـ. قال الشيخ اسمعيل : ويؤيده ما سبق من [Book of Prayer - Chapter on Conditions of Prayer] If one intends Asr without qualification, there is a difference: in al-Zahiriyyah: if one intends Zuhr, it is not valid because this time, just as it accepts the Zuhr of this day, it also accepts another Zuhr. And it is said: it is valid, and that is the correct (view) because the time is specific to it. This is if it is a current prayer. If it is a make-up prayer, and he prays after the time has exited while he does not know of its exit, based on the permissibility of making up with the intention of current prayer. End quote. Then I found the author of al-Nahr said ... end quote. The words of Shaykh Isma'il, may Allah have mercy on him.
